Authentication options include Password Hash Sync (a hash of the hash), Pass-through Authentication, and Federation. Password Hash Sync is generally recommended so cloud authentications do not depend on on-premises availability.

Device joining options

  • Entra ID joined: Device authenticates to Entra — the tightest binding, typically corporate-owned.
  • Entra ID registered: Device is known to Entra (BYOD scenario) — enables some heightened trust.
  • Hybrid joined: Device is joined to AD DS and the device object is synchronized and registered to Entra. Windows 7 and above can support hybrid join; Entra ID join and register are Windows 10 and above (iOS, Android, macOS support registration).

7. Authentication and Authorization

Authentication must happen first — the user must prove they are who they say they are. Authorization then decides what they can access.

Authentication methods

  • Password only: The weakest option. Passwords are a shared secret that can be stolen, guessed, or phished.
  • Multifactor authentication (MFA): Uses two or more factors from different categories: something you know (password, PIN), something you have (phone, hardware token), something you are (biometric).
  • Passwordless: No password is used at all.

Passwordless and passkeys

  • Microsoft Authenticator app: Can be used passwordlessly — the app shows a number to match, with location and application context to prevent phishing.
  • Passkeys (FIDO2): Strong, phishing-resistant authentication based on a proximity requirement. The passkey device (such as a phone) must be physically near (typically via Bluetooth) the device requesting authentication, so a remote attacker cannot trigger it. The Authenticator app supports passkeys for Entra. Windows Hello for Business uses a FIDO2-based passkey.

Security defaults

Security defaults are a baseline policy in Entra ID that enforces MFA for all users, requires MFA for administrators, and requires MFA for specific risky activities. Useful for organizations that do not have Conditional Access licenses (Entra ID P1 or higher).

Conditional Access

Conditional Access is the primary authorization mechanism in Entra. It evaluates signals about a sign-in and applies controls before issuing a token. Key elements:

  • Signals / conditions: User or group membership, role, location, device platform, device state, user risk, sign-in risk, insider risk, client app, authentication context, terms of use.
  • Decisions / controls: Allow, block, require MFA, require a specific authentication strength (e.g., phishing-resistant), require terms of use acceptance, require a password change, require a compliant device.

Role-based access control (RBAC)

RBAC assigns a role (a set of permissions) to an identity at a specific scope. RBAC exists in Entra, Azure, Microsoft 365, and many other services. Built-in roles are pre-defined (e.g., Global Administrator, User Administrator), and custom roles can be created. Following Zero Trust, always grant the smallest role that does the job.

Password protection

Entra ID provides global banned password lists (Microsoft-maintained weak passwords) and custom banned password lists (organization-specific terms such as company or product names). These can be enforced on both Entra ID and on-premises AD DS. Other password protection capabilities include smart lockout (against password-spraying attacks) and self-service password reset (SSPR), which lets users reset their own passwords after verifying one or more methods.

8. Identity Governance

Identity governance covers the full lifecycle of an identity inside an organization.

Joiner / Mover / Leaver lifecycle

Identity governance automates actions across the user lifecycle using lifecycle workflows. The user's start date and end date act as triggers — for example, sending a welcome email a week before start, generating a one-time passcode on day one, or removing access and adding the user to an alumni distribution list on the day they leave.

Dynamic groups

Dynamic groups automatically add or remove users based on user properties (department, job title, etc.). They are a powerful complement to lifecycle workflows.

Access reviews

Access reviews periodically check whether users still need access to groups, applications, or roles. Reviews can be performed by a designated reviewer or as self-reviews. They help ensure that users do not retain permissions they no longer need.

Privileged Identity Management (PIM)

PIM provides just-in-time elevation to privileged roles. A user is eligible for a role but is not active in it by default. When they need it, they activate the role for a defined time window after passing stronger authentication. The elevation is temporary and removed automatically.

Identity Protection

Identity Protection evaluates many signals to calculate risk levels:

  • User risk: Aggregate risk for the identity — for example, the user's password appearing on the dark web.
  • Sign-in risk: Risk of a specific sign-in event — for example, a sign-in from a country and device the user has never used before.

These risk signals can be consumed by Conditional Access policies to require MFA, password changes, or block the sign-in entirely.

Permissions Management

Permissions Management (now Microsoft Entra Permissions Management) discovers what permissions an identity has across Azure, AWS, and GCP. It identifies unused permissions, recommends removals, and continuously monitors for excess privilege. It is a cross-cloud permissions governance solution.

Entra Private Access and Internet Access

Microsoft's global secure access client, installed on the device, facilitates two capabilities:

  • Entra Private Access: Replaces traditional VPN for accessing private network resources. Traffic for any TCP or UDP application is redirected to the Entra edge, where Conditional Access is evaluated, and then forwarded to the resource. Aligns with Zero Trust instead of granting blanket network access.
  • Entra Internet Access: Secures outbound internet traffic. Can validate fully qualified domain names and categories, blocking access to risky destinations.

Entra Suite

The Entra Suite bundles advanced capabilities on top of an Entra ID P1 license: it adds P2 features, the rich access reviews beyond P2, lifecycle workflows, private access, internet access, face check with Verified ID, and identity protection. Designed for organizations that want a single bundle for identity governance, network access, and verification.

9. Azure Infrastructure Security

Azure is the cloud, available in many regions, where virtual machines, Kubernetes clusters, app services, storage accounts, and databases can be deployed.

DDoS Protection

DDoS protection defends against distributed denial-of-service attacks. Two tiers are available:

  • DDoS Basic: Free, automatic, and aimed at very high-volume attacks only — not tuned to the application.
  • DDoS Standard: Paid tier tuned to the specific application. Uses machine learning to learn expected traffic patterns, supports custom policies, traffic monitoring, alerting, and access to support. Two scopes are available:
    • Network: Protects all public-facing resources in a virtual network.
    • IP: Protects specific public IP addresses.

Azure Firewall

Azure Firewall is a managed stateful firewall service that works at both Layer 4 (network) and Layer 7 (application):

  • Layer 7: Application rules that understand HTTP, fully qualified domain names, and can perform TLS inspection using a trusted certificate.
  • Layer 4: Network rules that understand TCP/UDP and packet flows.

It also includes threat intelligence feeds, can inspect traffic in any direction, and provides centralized logging.

Web Application Firewall (WAF)

WAF protects against common web exploits using the OWASP Core Rule Set (CRS): SQL injection, cross-site scripting, HTTP floods, and other Layer 7 DDoS attacks. WAF can be deployed:

  • Globally: With Azure Front Door.
  • Regionally: With Azure Application Gateway.

Virtual Networks and Network Security Groups

A virtual network (vNet) lives in a specific region within a subscription and is a boundary of isolation — vNets cannot talk to each other by default. Peering can be used to connect vNets. Within a vNet, subnets can be created.

Network Security Groups (NSGs) are sets of rules based on source/destination IP address, port, and protocol (TCP/UDP). NSGs are typically assigned to subnets (preferred) or directly to network interfaces. They allow or deny traffic and are the primary tool for additional segmentation inside a vNet.

Azure Virtual Network Manager

Azure Virtual Network Manager provides centralized network management. From a security perspective, it offers Security Admin Rules:

  • Look similar to NSG rules but are centrally managed.
  • Processed before NSGs (act as a funnel).
  • Support Always Allow — bypasses the NSG entirely. Useful to guarantee critical traffic (patching infrastructure, domain controllers) is never blocked.
  • Support Deny — traffic is killed before reaching the NSG.

Azure Bastion

Azure Bastion is a managed jump box deployed inside the vNet. It enables RDP and SSH access to virtual machines without exposing public IP addresses, eliminating port scanning and reducing exposure to zero-day exploits. Higher SKUs (Standard, Premium) add features such as SSH-to-Windows and connecting to VMs by IP or in peered vNets.

Azure Key Vault (recap)

Azure Key Vault stores secrets (read/write), keys (import or generate, no export, run crypto operations inside), and certificates (full lifecycle). Standard tier uses software-protected keys; Premium uses HSMs.

10. Threat Protection and Monitoring

Microsoft Defender for Cloud

Defender for Cloud is a cloud-native application protection platform (CNAPP) that works across Azure, AWS, and GCP. It is built around three pillars:

  • Cloud Security Posture Management (CSPM): Understand the state of the cloud. Built on Azure Policy initiatives (such as the free Microsoft Cloud Security Benchmark). Generates a secure score, recommendations prioritized by risk, and regulatory compliance views.
  • Cloud Workload Protection Platform (CWPP): Defender plans for specific workloads (Defender for Storage, Defender for Containers, Defender for Key Vault) plus core protections such as just-in-time VM access and adaptive network/application controls.
  • DevSecOps: Shift security left by integrating it earlier in the development pipeline.

Microsoft Sentinel

Microsoft Sentinel is a cloud-native SIEM and SOAR solution. It collects signals from agents, diagnostic settings, syslog, and other sources into a Log Analytics workspace, then detects, investigates, and responds to threats.

  • SIEM: Security Information and Event Management — collect, detect, investigate.
  • SOAR: Security Orchestration Automated Response — automation playbooks.

Costs are based on the volume of data ingested into the Log Analytics workspace plus the chosen retention.

Microsoft Security Copilot

Security Copilot is an AI assistant built on a large language model. It is integrated into services such as Sentinel, Entra, Intune, and Defender in two ways:

  • Embedded: A Copilot icon appears inside the portal of the product.
  • Immersive: A standalone prompt experience that works across all integrated services.

Microsoft Defender XDR

Defender XDR is an extended detection and response suite that unifies protection across multiple domains. Its portal at security.microsoft.com has been merged with Sentinel. The suite includes:

  • Defender for Office 365: Email and collaboration protection — detects malicious links, QR codes, and runs attachments in a detonation chamber.
  • Defender for Endpoint: Unified endpoint prevention, detection, and response with malware protection and post-event investigation.
  • Defender for Cloud Apps: Discovers and governs SaaS usage, including third-party apps and proxy-fed signals.
  • Defender for Identity: Monitors on-premises AD DS and AD FS signals to detect compromised identities.
  • Defender Vulnerability Management: Continuous asset visibility and exposure assessment for internet-facing resources.
  • Threat intelligence: Reports and context about threats to consider in the environment.

11. Compliance and Data Governance

Six principles of compliance

  • Control: The customer has control over the privacy of their data, with tools and visibility to make informed decisions.
  • Transparency: Clear information about what data is collected so customers can make informed decisions.
  • Security: Strong security and encryption protect the customer's data.
  • Legal protections: Local privacy laws are honored and the customer has clear legal rights — including Microsoft's willingness to fight legal demands that would compromise customer data.
  • No content-based targeting: Email, chat, files, and personal content are not used to target advertising.
  • Benefit to the customer: Any data collected should benefit the customer and improve their experience.

Service Trust Portal

The Service Trust Portal (servicetrust.microsoft.com) hosts compliance documentation, certifications, reference materials, standards, reports, regional and industry information, and white papers. Customers can build a personal library of the documents most relevant to them.

Microsoft Priva

Microsoft Priva focuses on personal data privacy. It includes two main solutions:

  • Privacy Risk Management: Discovers where private data lives (in Exchange Online, SharePoint Online, OneDrive for Business, Teams) and helps limit its transfer across regional or departmental boundaries.
  • Subject Rights Requests: Handles the complete workflow for individuals requesting access to or deletion of their personal data, with workflow automation and reporting.

Microsoft Purview

Microsoft Purview is the unified solution for governance, compliance, and data security. Key components include:

  • Compliance Manager: Tracks compliance posture with a compliance score, assessments (groupings of controls from a specific regulation), improvement actions with point values and impact, and assignments to individuals for accountability.
  • Data lifecycle management: Classifiers (built-in and custom trainable classifiers plus sensitive info types), retention policies, and records management.
  • Information protection: Sensitivity labels that classify data (highly confidential, public, personal, top secret) and can apply actions such as watermarks, encryption, and access restrictions. A single item has a single label.
  • Data Loss Prevention (DLP): Policies to prevent risky movement of sensitive data.

Data lifecycle

Microsoft Purview supports a five-step data lifecycle:

  • Know: Discover where the data is across the organization.
  • Classify: Identify the sensitivity of the data using built-in or custom classifications.
  • Protect: Encrypt, add access restrictions, apply watermarks.
  • Prevent: Use DLP to detect and stop risky behavior such as inappropriate copying.
  • Govern: Retain or delete data automatically based on requirements.

Sensitivity labels, retention, and records

  • Sensitivity labels: Classify and protect — metadata in clear text that travels with the item, can trigger encryption, watermarks, or access controls.
  • Retention policies: Retain content for a defined period and delete it afterward.
  • Records management: Apply restrictions to content labeled as a record (activities blocked, all actions logged, proof of disposition at end of retention).

Insider Risk Management

Insider Risk Management defines policies for internal risk signals. When behavior matches a policy, an alert is generated. Analysts then dismiss the alert or create a case for further investigation.

eDiscovery

eDiscovery finds content across mailboxes, groups, Teams, SharePoint, OneDrive, Skype, and Yammer. Three tiers exist:

  • Content search: Basic keyword search and export.
  • eDiscovery Standard: Adds case management, legal holds, and search/export.
  • eDiscovery Premium: Adds the complete end-to-end workflow with advanced analytics and custodian management.

Audit

Audit logs capture Microsoft 365 operations for forensic evidence, compliance, regulations, and internal investigations. The default retention is 90 days for Audit Standard and one year for Audit Premium. Premium also provides a higher-bandwidth API for faster access. All three access methods — UI, command line, and API — are available in both tiers.

Section Summary

1. Shared Responsibility Model

  • On-premises: Customer manages everything — physical hardware, OS, applications, data, identities. Even with a managed service provider, accountability remains with the customer
  • IaaS: Provider handles physical infrastructure, hypervisor, and hosts. Customer manages from OS upward: operating systems, applications, identity, data, networking configuration
  • PaaS: Provider manages OS, runtime, and middleware. Customer responsible for data, devices, identities, and application configuration. Shared responsibility in application layer
  • SaaS: Provider manages application, network, OS, and infrastructure. Customer manages only identities, devices, and identity infrastructure (like on-premises AD sync components)
  • Always retained: Identities (user accounts, service principals, managed identities), devices (endpoints), and data (classification, retention, protection) remain customer responsibility across all models

2. Defense in Depth & CIA Triad

  • Seven layers: Physical (locks, guards, cameras) → Identity (primary perimeter in cloud) → Perimeter (DDoS protection) → Network (segmentation, isolation) → Compute (host firewalls, anti-malware, patching) → Application (secure code, no exploitable vulnerabilities) → Data (most critical asset)
  • CIA Triad: Confidentiality (encryption, access controls — sensitive data only accessible to authorized), Integrity (data in correct state, no tampering), Availability (data accessible when needed). Security must balance with business function
  • Common threats: Data breach (theft of organizational data), dictionary attacks (brute-force common passwords), ransomware (encrypts data, demands payment), DDoS (floods services), phishing (trick users into clicking malicious links), spear phishing (targeted phishing against specific individuals)

3. Zero Trust

  • Core assumption: Network cannot be trusted. Being on internal network does not mean safe. Trust is never implicit — every access is verified
  • Verify explicitly: Every access attempt performs authentication and authorization. Checks identity, device, location, and data classification
  • Least privilege: Minimum permissions needed for a role. Implement Just Enough Administration (JEA) and Just in Time (JIT) elevation — heightened permissions only when needed
  • Assume breach: Act as though attacker is already on network. Segment network, monitor signals continuously, allow only required traffic, limit blast radius
  • Seven pillars: Identities (primary control point), Devices (large attack surface if unsecured), Applications (consume and generate data), Data (discovered, classified, protected), Infrastructure (compute, storage, services), Networks (segmentation, isolation), Visibility (continuous monitoring)

4. Encryption & Hashing

  • Symmetric encryption: Same key encrypts and decrypts. Challenge: securely sharing the key — if intercepted, key can decrypt data
  • Asymmetric encryption: Key pair — private key (kept secret) and public key (shared). Sender encrypts with recipient's public key; only recipient's private key can decrypt. Keys mathematically linked
  • Digital signatures: Sender hashes data, encrypts hash with private key to create signature. Receiver hashes data, decrypts signature with sender's public key, compares. Match = data not tampered, sender verified
  • Hashing: Input of any size → fixed-size output (hash). Same input always produces same hash. Used to store passwords securely (hash stored, not plaintext)
  • Salting: Per-user random value added to password before hashing. Produces unique hash for each user, making precomputed hash tables (rainbow tables) useless
  • Azure Key Vault: Managed Azure resource. Secrets (read/write: passwords, connection strings), Keys (import/generate, no export, crypto operations inside vault), Certificates (TLS/SSL lifecycle). Standard (software encryption) vs Premium (HSM-protected keys)

5. GRC Concepts

  • Governance: Rules, practices, and processes for organizational activities. Often based on regulatory requirements for specific industry or country
  • Risk: Identifying, assessing, and responding to threats. Can be external (malicious actors) or internal (insider threats)
  • Compliance: Adherence to country, region, federal, or industry-specific requirements for data handling
  • Data residency: Physical/geographic location where data must live
  • Data sovereignty: Which country's laws apply to stored data
  • Data privacy: What data is stored and how it is used

6. Identity Fundamentals

  • Identity types: User identities (carbon-based life forms), Application/workload identities (service principals with secret/certificate, or managed identities with no secrets), Device identities (send signals, must be verified)
  • Four pillars: Administration (basic management), Authentication (proving "who I am"), Authorization (determining "what I can do"), Audit (tracking "what I have done")
  • Modern authentication: Centralized identity provider (IdP) like Microsoft Entra ID. Speaks web protocols, issues tokens, provides risk detection and auditing
  • Protocols: OAuth 2.0 (authorization for delegated access), OpenID Connect (built on OAuth 2.0, provides identity), SAML (federation, exchange identity information)
  • SSO & federation: SSO = authenticate once, access all services trusting same IdP. Federation = trust between different IdPs (different Entra tenants, Entra and Google, Entra and on-premises SAML)
  • User types: Internal (created in tenant, employee), External/guest (from another tenant, authenticates against own IdP, uses federation)
  • AD DS vs Entra ID: AD DS = on-premises, hierarchical with OUs, uses Kerberos/NTLM. Entra ID = cloud-based, speaks modern protocols (OAuth, OIDC, SAML)
  • Hybrid identity: Sync AD DS (source of truth) to Entra ID. Entra Connect (on-premises sync engine) or Entra Cloud Sync (cloud-based, future direction). Auth options: Password Hash Sync (recommended, hash of hash), Pass-through Authentication, Federation
  • Device joining: Entra ID joined (tightest binding, corporate-owned), Entra ID registered (BYOD, known to Entra), Hybrid joined (joined to AD DS, synced to Entra). Windows 7+ supports hybrid; Entra join/register requires Windows 10+ (iOS/Android/macOS support registration)

7. Authentication & Authorization

  • Authentication methods: Password only (weakest, shared secret), MFA (two+ factors from different categories), Passwordless (no password at all)
  • MFA factors: Something you know (password, PIN), something you have (phone, hardware token), something you are (biometric)
  • Passwordless: Microsoft Authenticator (number matching, location/app context), Passkeys/FIDO2 (phishing-resistant, proximity requirement via Bluetooth, Authenticator supports passkeys), Windows Hello for Business (FIDO2-based)
  • Security defaults: Baseline policy enforcing MFA for all users, required for admins, required for risky activities. For organizations without Conditional Access licenses (Entra ID P1+)
  • Conditional Access: Primary authorization mechanism. Evaluates signals (user/group, role, location, device platform/state, user/sign-in/insider risk, client app, auth context, terms of use) and applies controls (allow, block, require MFA, require auth strength, require terms of use, require password change, require compliant device)
  • RBAC: Role (set of permissions) assigned to identity at specific scope. Built-in roles (Global Admin, User Admin) or custom roles. Always grant smallest role that does the job (Zero Trust)
  • Password protection: Global banned password lists (Microsoft-maintained), custom banned lists (org-specific terms), enforced on Entra ID and on-premises AD DS. Smart lockout (against password-spraying), SSPR (self-service password reset after verifying methods)

8. Identity Governance

  • Joiner/Mover/Leaver: Lifecycle workflows automate actions across user lifecycle. Start/end dates as triggers — welcome email before start, one-time passcode on day one, remove access and add to alumni list on departure
  • Dynamic groups: Automatically add/remove users based on properties (department, job title). Complement to lifecycle workflows
  • Access reviews: Periodic checks whether users still need access to groups, apps, or roles. Designated reviewer or self-review. Ensures users don't retain unnecessary permissions
  • PIM: Just-in-time elevation to privileged roles. User eligible but not active by default. Activate for defined time window after stronger authentication. Temporary, automatically removed
  • Identity Protection: Evaluates signals to calculate risk. User risk (aggregate, e.g., password on dark web), Sign-in risk (per-event, e.g., sign-in from unfamiliar country/device). Risk signals feed Conditional Access (require MFA, password change, or block)
  • Permissions Management: Discovers permissions across Azure, AWS, GCP. Identifies unused permissions, recommends removals, continuously monitors for excess privilege. Cross-cloud governance
  • Entra Private Access: Replaces traditional VPN. TCP/UDP traffic redirected to Entra edge, Conditional Access evaluated, then forwarded. Zero Trust instead of blanket network access
  • Entra Internet Access: Secures outbound internet traffic. Validates FQDNs and categories, blocks risky destinations
  • Entra Suite: Bundles advanced capabilities on top of P1: adds P2 features, rich access reviews, lifecycle workflows, private/internet access, face check with Verified ID, identity protection. Single bundle for governance, network access, verification

9. Azure Infrastructure Security

  • DDoS Protection: Basic (free, automatic, high-volume only, not tuned to app) vs Standard (paid, ML-tuned to specific app, custom policies, monitoring, alerting, support). Standard scopes: Network (all public IPs in vNet) or IP (specific IPs)
  • Azure Firewall: Managed stateful firewall at Layer 4 (network rules, TCP/UDP) and Layer 7 (application rules, HTTP, FQDNs, TLS inspection). Threat intelligence feeds, inspects traffic in any direction, centralized logging
  • WAF: Protects against OWASP Core Rule Set exploits (SQL injection, XSS, HTTP floods). Deployed globally with Azure Front Door or regionally with Azure Application Gateway
  • Virtual Networks: Regional isolation boundary within subscription. vNets cannot communicate by default; peering connects them. Subnets created within vNets
  • NSGs: Rules based on source/destination IP, port, protocol (TCP/UDP). Assigned to subnets (preferred) or network interfaces. Primary tool for segmentation inside vNet
  • Virtual Network Manager: Centralized network management. Security Admin Rules look like NSG rules but centrally managed, processed before NSGs (funnel). Support Always Allow (bypasses NSG, guarantees critical traffic) and Deny (kills traffic before NSG)
  • Azure Bastion: Managed jump box inside vNet. RDP/SSH to VMs without public IPs, eliminating port scanning and reducing zero-day exposure. Higher SKUs (Standard, Premium) add SSH-to-Windows, connect by IP, peered vNets

10. Threat Protection & Monitoring

  • Defender for Cloud: CNAPP across Azure, AWS, GCP. Three pillars: CSPM (understand cloud state, Azure Policy initiatives like free MCSB, secure score, recommendations, regulatory compliance), CWPP (Defender plans for specific workloads like Storage/Containers/Key Vault, JIT VM access, adaptive controls), DevSecOps (shift security left into development pipeline)
  • Microsoft Sentinel: Cloud-native SIEM and SOAR. Collects signals from agents, diagnostic settings, syslog into Log Analytics workspace. SIEM = collect, detect, investigate. SOAR = automation playbooks. Costs based on data volume ingested plus retention
  • Security Copilot: AI assistant on large language model. Integrated into Sentinel, Entra, Intune, Defender. Embedded (Copilot icon inside product portal) or Immersive (standalone prompt experience across all services)
  • Defender XDR: Extended detection and response suite at security.microsoft.com (merged with Sentinel). Includes: Defender for Office 365 (email/collaboration, malicious links/QR codes, detonation chamber), Defender for Endpoint (unified prevention/detection/response, malware protection, post-event investigation), Defender for Cloud Apps (SaaS discovery/governance, third-party apps, proxy signals), Defender for Identity (on-premises AD DS/AD FS signals, compromised identities), Defender Vulnerability Management (continuous asset visibility, exposure assessment), Threat intelligence (reports and context)

11. Compliance & Data Governance

  • Six principles: Control (customer controls privacy, tools and visibility), Transparency (clear info about data collection), Security (strong encryption), Legal protections (local privacy laws honored, Microsoft fights compromising legal demands), No content-based targeting (email/chat/files not used for advertising), Benefit to customer (collected data benefits customer)
  • Service Trust Portal: servicetrust.microsoft.com hosts compliance documentation, certifications, standards, reports, regional/industry info, white papers. Customers build personal library of relevant documents
  • Microsoft Priva: Personal data privacy. Privacy Risk Management (discovers where private data lives in Exchange/SharePoint/OneDrive/Teams, limits transfer across boundaries), Subject Rights Requests (complete workflow for access/deletion requests, automation and reporting)
  • Microsoft Purview: Unified governance, compliance, and data security. Compliance Manager (compliance score, assessments, improvement actions with point values, assignments), Data lifecycle management (classifiers, retention policies, records), Information protection (sensitivity labels with watermarks/encryption/access restrictions, single label per item), DLP (prevent risky movement of sensitive data)
  • Data lifecycle: Five steps — Know (discover where data is), Classify (identify sensitivity), Protect (encrypt, restrict access, watermark), Prevent (DLP to detect/stop risky behavior), Govern (retain or delete automatically)
  • Sensitivity labels: Classify and protect. Clear-text metadata travels with item, can trigger encryption/watermarks/access controls
  • Retention & records: Retention policies (retain for defined period, then delete). Records management (restrictions on labeled records, activities blocked, all actions logged, proof of disposition at end)
  • Insider Risk Management: Policies for internal risk signals. Behavior matches policy → alert generated. Analysts dismiss alert or create case for investigation
  • eDiscovery: Finds content across mailboxes, groups, Teams, SharePoint, OneDrive, Skype, Yammer. Content search (basic keyword), Standard (case management, legal holds), Premium (end-to-end workflow, advanced analytics, custodian management)
  • Audit: Logs M365 operations for forensic evidence, compliance, regulations, investigations. Standard (90-day retention), Premium (1-year retention, higher-bandwidth API). UI, CLI, and API access in both tiers

Key Concepts

  • Shared Responsibility: Customer always retains identities, devices, and data regardless of service model; provider takes on more as you move from IaaS to SaaS
  • Defense in Depth: Seven layers (physical, identity, perimeter, network, compute, application, data) protecting the CIA triad (Confidentiality, Integrity, Availability)
  • Zero Trust: Verify explicitly, least privilege (JEA/JIT), assume breach applied across seven pillars: identities, devices, apps, data, infrastructure, networks, visibility
  • Symmetric vs Asymmetric Encryption: Symmetric uses one shared key; asymmetric uses a public/private key pair for secure communication
  • Hashing and Salting: Hashing produces fixed-size output for integrity verification; salt adds per-user randomness to prevent dictionary attacks
  • Azure Key Vault: Stores secrets (read/write values), keys (non-exportable cryptographic material), and certificates (TLS/SSL lifecycle management)
  • Four Pillars of Identity: Administration, Authentication (proving who I am), Authorization (what I can do), and Audit (what I have done)
  • Authentication Protocols: OAuth 2.0 (authorization), OpenID Connect (identity on OAuth 2.0), SAML (federation between identity providers)
  • Hybrid Identity: Entra Connect (on-premises sync engine) vs Cloud Sync (cloud-based, future direction); PHS, PTA, or federation for authentication
  • Conditional Access: Evaluates signals (user, location, device, risk) and applies controls (MFA, block, compliant device) before issuing a token
  • PIM (Privileged Identity Management): Just-in-time role elevation with eligible assignments activated on demand for a defined time window
  • DDoS Protection Tiers: Network Protection (all public IPs in a vNet) or IP Protection (specific IPs) with ML tuning and alerting
  • Defender for Cloud Pillars: CSPM (posture and secure score), CWPP (workload threat protection), DevSecOps (shift-left security in CI/CD)
  • Microsoft Sentinel: Cloud-native SIEM (collect, detect, investigate) and SOAR (automated response with playbooks) on Log Analytics workspace
  • Compliance Principles: Control, Transparency, Security, Legal protections, No content-based targeting, Benefit to customer; supported by STP, Priva, and Purview

Georgia Kalyva SC-900 Video

Official Microsoft Learn Video Series — All 6 Videos, Condensed

Module: Georgia Kalyva Microsoft Learn Video Series

6 Videos | Official Microsoft Learn SC-900 Training

1. Introduction to Security, Compliance, and Identity Concepts

Shared Responsibility Model

The pizza analogy is key: On-premises = make pizza from scratch (customer does everything). IaaS = buy pizza base (provider: data center, servers; customer: OS, apps, data). PaaS = partially prepared pizza (provider: runtime/OS; customer: apps, data). SaaS = delivered pizza (provider: everything; customer: identities, devices, data).
Critical: The customer always retains responsibility for data, devices, and identities regardless of service model.

Defense in Depth

Layered security strategy — an onion, not a single wall. Seven layers: Physical security → Identity & access → Perimeter (DDoS) → Network (segmentation) → Compute (VM hardening) → Application → Data (encryption). Each layer slows attackers; if one fails, the next catches them.

CIA Triad

  • Confidentiality: Data seen only by authorized people (encryption, access permissions)
  • Integrity: Data accurate and trustworthy (hashing, validation, auditing)
  • Availability: Data accessible when needed (redundancy, backups, resilience)

Balance all three — focusing on one alone is not enough.

Zero Trust

Never trust, always verify. Three guiding principles: Verify explicitly (check identity, device, location, behavior), Least privilege (JEA/JIT), Assume breach (segment, limit blast radius). Applied across six foundational pillars: identities, devices, applications, data, infrastructure, and networks.

Encryption

  • Symmetric: Same key to encrypt/decrypt — efficient for large data
  • Asymmetric: Public/private key pair — used for TLS, digital signatures

Protects data at rest (stored), in transit (moving), and in use (processed).

Hashing and Salting

Hashing: Fixed-length output, deterministic (same input → same hash), one-way (no decryption). Used to store passwords securely. Salt: A per-user random value added before hashing so identical passwords produce different hashes, defeating precomputed dictionary/rainbow table attacks.

GRC (Governance, Risk, Compliance)

  • Governance: Rules, policies, oversight — who can access what
  • Risk management: Identify and respond to threats (cyberattacks, data leaks, fraud)
  • Compliance: Follow laws/regulations (GDPR, industry-specific standards)

Related concepts: Data residency (geographic location), Data sovereignty (which country's laws apply), Data privacy (what data is stored and how it is used).

Identity as the New Security Perimeter

Four pillars: Administration (create/manage identities), Authentication (prove identity via MFA, passwordless), Authorization (what you can access, least privilege), Audit (track who did what).

Authentication = proving who you are. Authorization = what you can do once signed in.

Identity Provider (IdP): Central service for authentication. Enables SSO, MFA, federation. Federation: Trust between identity providers — users authenticate with their own IdP.

Directory services: Central address book for identities. Active Directory DS = on-premises; Microsoft Entra ID = cloud evolution.

2. Introduction to Microsoft Entra

Microsoft Entra ID Overview

Cloud-based identity and access management (IAM) service. Acts as central identity system for cloud and on-premises apps. An Entra tenant = directory representing one organization. Manages human identities (employees, guests), workload identities (service principals, managed identities), and device identities.

Hybrid Identity

Single identity across on-premises and cloud. Two sync tools: Entra Connect (sync engine runs on-premises) and Entra Cloud Sync (runs in the cloud, future direction). Authentication options: Password Hash Sync (recommended, no on-premises dependency), Pass-through Authentication, Federation.

Authentication Methods

  • Traditional: Passwords (weak alone)
  • Phone-based: SMS, voice calls, OATH tokens
  • Passwordless: Windows Hello for Business, Microsoft Authenticator app, FIDO2 security keys, certificate-based auth

MFA: Combines two+ factors — something you know (password), something you have (phone), something you are (biometric). Security Defaults: Baseline MFA enforcement without premium licenses.

Password Protection

Global banned password list: Always-on, Microsoft-maintained. Custom banned password list: Organization-specific terms. Extends to on-premises AD in hybrid environments. Also features: smart lockout, SSPR.

Conditional Access

Smart if-then decision engine: evaluates signals (user, location, device, app, risk) and applies controls (block, grant, require MFA, require compliant device, session controls). Example: finance employee traveling → unusual location → policy requires MFA + compliant device.

Global Secure Access

Unifies Identity + Network + Endpoint controls. Includes Entra Internet Access (secures SaaS and web traffic) and Entra Private Access (replaces legacy VPN for private resources). Uses a lightweight client on devices.

RBAC (Role-Based Access Control)

Built-in roles: Global Administrator, User Administrator, Security Administrator, etc. Entra RBAC controls identity resources; Azure RBAC controls Azure infrastructure (VMs, storage). Custom roles for flexibility. Always apply least privilege.

Identity Governance

Joiner/Mover/Leaver lifecycle: automated using lifecycle workflows. Dynamic groups: auto-add/remove based on user attributes. Access reviews: periodic recertification of access. PIM (Privileged Identity Management): just-in-time elevation to privileged roles, time-bound, requires MFA + approval, fully audited.

Identity Protection

Analyzes trillions of signals to detect user risk (leaked credentials) and sign-in risk (atypical travel, anonymous IP). Risks can trigger automated remediation (MFA, password reset, block). Integrates with Conditional Access and Security Copilot.

Security Copilot in Entra

Embedded in Risky Users report: summarizes risk level, highlights triggers, explains in natural language. Available as standalone experience and embedded in Entra portal.

3. Microsoft Security Solutions: Part 1 (Copilot + Infrastructure)

Microsoft Security Copilot

AI-powered security analysis tool combining LLMs with a Microsoft security-specific model. Integrates with Microsoft and non-Microsoft sources. Available in two modes: Standalone (dedicated portal) and Embedded (inside products like Sentinel, Defender, Entra).

Key Terminology

  • Session: A single conversation with context
  • Prompt: A question or instruction entered in the prompt bar
  • Capabilities: Specialized functions for security tasks (analyze incidents, query logs)
  • Plugins: Connect Copilot to Microsoft or third-party data sources
  • Workspaces: Separate Copilot environments within a tenant (per team, role, or regulation)
  • Orchestrator: The "brain" that combines capabilities + plugins to answer prompts
  • Agents: AI-powered assistants that autonomously handle high-volume repetitive tasks

Effective Prompting

Structure: Goal (what you need), Context (why/for whom), Expectations (format/detail), Sources (where to look). Good prompts reduce back-and-forth and yield consistent results.

Azure DDoS Protection

  • Network Protection: Full-featured, all public IPs in a vNet
  • IP Protection: Per-IP coverage
  • All Azure services get default infrastructure-level protection
  • Always-on monitoring, adaptive tuning, alerts via Azure Monitor

Azure Firewall

Managed stateful firewall. Supports Layer 7 (application rules, FQDNs, TLS inspection) and Layer 4 (network rules, TCP/UDP). Uses Microsoft Threat Intelligence. Deployed in hub-spoke topology for centralized control.

Web Application Firewall (WAF)

Protects web apps from SQL injection, XSS, and application-layer DDoS. Uses OWASP Core Rule Set. Deployed with: Azure Front Door (global) or Azure Application Gateway (regional).

Virtual Networks and NSGs

VNet: Private network for Azure resources, provides isolation. Subnets: Further segmentation within a VNet. Network Security Groups (NSGs): Traffic filters based on source/destination, port, protocol, priority. First match wins. Default rules cannot be removed but can be overridden with higher-priority rules (priority 100-4096).

Azure Bastion

Managed jump box inside the VNet. Enables RDP/SSH to VMs without public IPs, directly from the Azure portal over TLS. No special client needed. Reduces port scanning and zero-day exploit exposure.

Azure Key Vault

Centrally stores secrets (passwords, API keys), keys (non-exportable, crypto operations inside), and certificates (full lifecycle). Two tiers: Standard (software encryption) and Premium (HSM-backed). Access tightly controlled with auth and authorization.

4. Microsoft Security Solutions: Part 2 (Defender for Cloud + Sentinel)

Microsoft Defender for Cloud

Cloud-native application protection platform (CNAPP) with three pillars:

  • CSPM (Cloud Security Posture Management): Continuous assessment, Secure Score, recommendations, compliance with MCSB. Foundational features free.
  • CWPP (Cloud Workload Protection Platform): Targeted threat protection for servers, containers, databases, storage. Delivered through per-workload Defender plans.
  • DevSecOps: Shift-left security — integrates with GitHub/Azure DevOps, analyzes IaC templates, prioritizes issues in code, supports remediation via PR annotations.

Security Policies and Initiatives

Microsoft Cloud Security Benchmark (MCSB): Default initiative with Microsoft's best practices. Policies define individual rules; initiatives group rules for scalable management. Non-compliant resources generate security recommendations.

Secure Score

Single score snapshot of overall risk level. Recommendations are grouped into security controls with point values. Fixing high-priority issues increases the score.

Microsoft Sentinel

Cloud-native SIEM (Security Information and Event Management — collect, detect, investigate) and SOAR (Security Orchestration Automated Response — automated playbooks).

Four Core Functions

  1. Collect: Data at cloud scale via built-in connectors (Microsoft/Azure), custom connectors, Syslog, REST APIs. Normalized using ASIM.
  2. Detect: Analytics rules group alerts into incidents. Maps to MITRE ATT&CK. Uses threat intelligence, watch lists, Workbooks.
  3. Investigate: Incidents as centralized case files. Proactive hunting with KQL queries. Notebooks for advanced analysis.
  4. Respond: Automation rules + playbooks (Azure Logic Apps). Actions: disable accounts, block traffic, create tickets.

Sentinel + Security Copilot

Two ways: Standalone (dedicated plugin) and Embedded (in Defender portal). Features: natural language to KQL, incident summarization, guided investigation flows using built-in prompt books.

MITRE ATT&CK

Publicly accessible knowledge base of attacker tactics and techniques. Sentinel maps analytics rules and detections to this framework for organized threat understanding.

5. Microsoft Security Solutions: Part 3 (Defender XDR)

Microsoft Defender XDR

Enterprise defense suite correlating signals across identities, devices, email, apps, data, and infrastructure. Presents a unified attack story in the Microsoft Defender portal instead of isolated alerts. Reduces investigation time via automatic correlation and threat intelligence enrichment.

Defender for Office 365

Protects email and collaboration (Teams, SharePoint). Key features: Safe Attachments (detonates in virtual environment), Safe Links, anti-phishing, anti-malware. Investigation tools: Explorer, Audit Log Search, Message Trace. Zero-hour auto-purge (ZAP): automatically removes malicious messages already delivered.

Defender for Endpoint

Comprehensive endpoint protection: behavioral sensors, cloud analytics, Microsoft Threat Intelligence. Covers laptops, desktops, servers. Next-gen AV, automated investigation and response.

Defender for Cloud Apps

Visibility and control over SaaS. Cloud Discovery: identifies shadow IT against 37,000+ app catalog. Assesses risk scores (security, compliance, legal). Controls: sanction/unsanction apps, block risky downloads, detect anomalous user behavior. SaaS Security Posture Management (SSPM) recommendations included.

Defender for Identity

Protects on-premises identity infrastructure (AD DS, AD FS). Lightweight sensors on domain controllers send signals to cloud for behavioral analysis. Detects privilege escalation, lateral movement, abnormal sign-ins. Remediation: disable accounts, force password resets from Defender portal.

Defender Vulnerability Management

Continuous asset discovery and vulnerability assessment across Windows, macOS, Linux, mobile, network devices. Risk-based prioritization using threat intelligence. Built-in remediation tracking from discovery to resolution.

Defender Threat Intelligence

Aggregates global threat data with Microsoft expertise. Tools: Threat Analytics (active campaigns), Intel Explorer (search IoCs, CVEs, keywords), Projects (organize indicators of compromise). Integration with Security Copilot for natural language threat summarization.

Microsoft Defender Portal

Unified security operations platform. Centralizes: exposure management (attack surface map), investigation & response (incidents, alerts, advanced hunting), threat intelligence, assets (devices, identities, apps), configuration management, and Secure Score. Integrates Sentinel, posture management, and Security Copilot.

6. Introduction to Microsoft Priva and Microsoft Purview

Service Trust Portal

Microsoft's public site (servicetrust.microsoft.com) for audit reports, certifications, standards, white papers. Publicly accessible; some sensitive documents require sign-in + NDA. Organized by certifications, reports, regional/industry materials, and tenant-specific resources.

Microsoft Privacy Principles

  1. Control: You stay in control of your data — collect, use, access, change, delete
  2. Transparency: Clear documentation of what data is collected and why
  3. Security: Encryption at rest and in transit
  4. Strong legal protections: Microsoft validates legal requests, redirects to customer when possible
  5. No content-based targeting: Emails, chats, files not used for advertising
  6. Benefit to customer: Data collection improves reliability and user experience

Microsoft Priva

Privacy automation solution. Capabilities:

  • Privacy Risk Management: Identifies data overexposure, risky transfers, over-retention
  • Subject Rights Requests: Automated workflow for access/deletion requests
  • Consent Management: Centralized capture and management of consumer consent
  • Tracker Scanning: Identifies tracking technologies on websites
  • Privacy Assessments: Automatically evaluates data processing activities

Microsoft Purview Information Protection

Sensitive information types: Pattern-based (credit cards, passport IDs). Exact data match (EDM): Compares against known data. Trainable classifiers: ML-based for contracts, invoices. Content Explorer: Snapshot of labeled data locations. Activity Explorer: Shows user actions with sensitive data over time.

Sensitivity Labels

Customizable, persistent (travel with content), clear-text metadata. Can encrypt, apply watermarks/headers/footers, or classify without protection. Auto-applied or recommended. Label policies: publish to users/groups, set default labels, require justification, enforce mandatory labeling. Extends to containers (SharePoint sites, M365 groups).

Data Loss Prevention (DLP)

Policies detect sensitive info types in Exchange, SharePoint, OneDrive, Teams, endpoints, cloud apps, Power BI. Actions: policy tips, block with override, block without override. Endpoint DLP extends to USB, printing, unapproved apps.

Insider Risk Management

Detects data leaks, IP theft, fraud, policy violations. Clear workflow: policies define risk indicators → alerts → triage → cases → remediation. Adaptive Protection: ML assesses user risk level and auto-adjusts DLP, retention, and Conditional Access controls accordingly.

Audit

  • Audit Standard: 90-day retention, enabled by default
  • Audit Premium: 1-year retention, custom policies, higher bandwidth API, intelligence insights

Searchable via Purview portal, CLI, or API. Security Copilot actions are also logged through Purview Audit.

eDiscovery

Find content across Exchange, Teams, OneDrive, SharePoint, Viva Engage. Workflow: search → place holds → review sets (analytics, tagging) → export. Three tiers: Content Search (basic), Standard (case management + holds), Premium (advanced analytics + custodian management). Copilot integration: summarize review sets, natural language to search queries.

Compliance Manager

Prebuilt assessments for regulations (ISO, GDPR). Compliance Score: shared responsibility view (Microsoft-managed + customer-managed actions). Improvement actions: step-by-step guidance, evidence upload, tracking, scoring. Points based on mandatory vs discretionary and preventative/detective/corrective classification.

Communication Compliance

Detects inappropriate/risky messages (offensive language, harassment, unauthorized sharing) across Microsoft and third-party platforms. Workflow: configure policy → review flagged messages → remediate (resolve, escalate, false positive). Copilot integration for message summarization.

Data Lifecycle Management

  • Retention labels: Item-level (one label per item), travel with content, auto-apply, support disposition review
  • Retention policies: Broad-level (entire mailbox/site), items inherit from container

Records Management

Content labeled as record: no edit/delete, all activities logged, proof of disposition. Regulatory records: strongest protection — label cannot be removed, retention cannot be shortened (even by admins).

Microsoft Purview Data Governance

Data Catalog organizes data into business domains (sales, finance), data products, and glossary terms. Federated governance model: data owners + stewards curate, central data office sets policies. Features: self-service data access, search/browse, health management, data quality.

Section Summary

1. Security, Compliance & Identity Concepts

  • Shared Responsibility: Customer always retains data, devices, and identities regardless of service model (IaaS/PaaS/SaaS). On-premises = full customer responsibility; SaaS = provider handles everything except identities/devices/data.
  • Defense in Depth: Seven layered controls (physical → identity → perimeter → network → compute → application → data) ensuring no single point of failure.
  • CIA Triad: Confidentiality (encryption/access control), Integrity (hashing/validation/auditing), Availability (redundancy/backups/resilience) — balance all three, never one alone.
  • Zero Trust: Verify explicitly (check identity, device, location, behavior), least privilege (JEA/JIT), assume breach (segment, limit blast radius). Six pillars: identities, devices, applications, data, infrastructure, networks.
  • Encryption: Symmetric (same key, efficient for bulk) vs Asymmetric (public/private pair, for TLS and digital signatures). Protects data at rest, in transit, and in use.
  • Hashing + Salt: One-way, deterministic, fixed-length. Salt adds per-user randomness so identical passwords produce different hashes, defeating rainbow tables.
  • GRC: Governance (policies and oversight), Risk management (identify/mitigate threats), Compliance (follow laws like GDPR). Data residency (geographic location), data sovereignty (applicable laws), data privacy (what/how data is used).
  • Identity Fundamentals: Authentication (proving identity) vs Authorization (what you can access). Four pillars: administration, authentication, authorization, auditing. IdP enables SSO, MFA, federation. AD DS = on-premises directory; Entra ID = cloud evolution.

2. Microsoft Entra

  • Entra ID: Cloud-based IAM, central identity system for cloud + on-premises. Tenant = directory representing one organization. Identity types: human (employees/guests), workload (service principals/managed identities), device.
  • Hybrid Identity: Entra Connect (on-premises sync engine) or Cloud Sync (cloud-based). Auth options: Password Hash Sync (recommended, no on-prem dependency), Pass-through Authentication, Federation.
  • Authentication Methods: Passwords (weak alone), phone-based (SMS, voice, OATH), passwordless (Windows Hello, Authenticator, FIDO2 keys, certificate-based). MFA combines knowledge/possession/inherence factors.
  • Security Defaults: Baseline MFA enforcement for organizations without P1/P2 licenses. Password Protection: Global banned list (always-on) + custom banned list (org-specific), extends to on-prem AD.
  • Conditional Access: If-then engine — signals (user group, location, device platform, risk level, client app) evaluated through assignments → access controls (block, grant with MFA, require compliant device, session controls like sign-in frequency).
  • Global Secure Access: SSE solution combining Entra Internet Access (SaaS/web security with tenant restrictions, content filtering) + Entra Private Access (replaces legacy VPN for private resources). Lightweight client on devices routes traffic through Entra edge.
  • RBAC: Built-in roles (Global Admin, User Admin, Security Admin, Billing Admin) + custom roles. Entra RBAC controls identity resources; Azure RBAC controls infrastructure (VMs, storage). Least privilege always.
  • Identity Governance: Lifecycle workflows (joiner/mover/leaver with triggers), dynamic groups (auto-add/remove by attributes), access reviews (periodic recertification, multi-stage up to 3 reviewers).
  • PIM: Just-in-time role elevation — eligible (not permanently active), activate on demand with MFA + business justification + approval, time-bound (e.g. 1 hour), fully logged and auditable.
  • Identity Protection: User risk (leaked credentials on dark web) + Sign-in risk (atypical travel, anonymous IP, unfamiliar properties). Automated remediation: MFA, password reset, block. Integrates with Conditional Access and Security Copilot.

3. Security Solutions Part 1 — Copilot & Azure Infrastructure

  • Security Copilot: AI-powered analysis combining LLMs with security-specific model. Available standalone (dedicated portal) or embedded (inside Sentinel, Defender, Entra). Plugin system connects to Microsoft and non-Microsoft sources.
  • Copilot Terminology: Session (conversation context), Prompt (question/instruction), Capabilities (specialized security functions), Plugins (data source connectors), Workspaces (per-team environments with own capacity and data residency), Orchestrator (combines capabilities + plugins), Agents (autonomous assistants for repetitive tasks).
  • Effective Prompting: Clear goal, context (why/for whom), expectations (format/detail), sources (where to look). Reduces back-and-forth and yields consistent results.
  • DDoS Protection: Network Protection (full-featured, all vNet public IPs) or IP Protection (per-IP). Default infrastructure-level protection for all Azure services. Always-on monitoring + adaptive tuning.
  • Azure Firewall: Managed stateful firewall. Layer 7 (application rules, FQDNs, TLS inspection) + Layer 4 (network rules, TCP/UDP). Uses Microsoft Threat Intelligence. Hub-spoke topology for centralized control.
  • WAF: OWASP Core Rule Set — protects against SQL injection, XSS, app-layer DDoS. Deployed via Azure Front Door (global) or Application Gateway (regional).
  • vNets & NSGs: VNet = private network, provides isolation. Subnets segment within a VNet. NSGs = traffic filters by source/destination/port/protocol, priority 100-4096, first match wins. Default rules exist but can be overridden.
  • Azure Bastion: Managed jump box inside VNet — RDP/SSH to VMs without public IPs, directly from portal over TLS. No special client needed. Reduces port scanning and zero-day exploit exposure.
  • Azure Key Vault: Central storage for secrets (passwords, connection strings), keys (non-exportable, crypto operations inside vault), certificates (full TLS/SSL lifecycle). Standard (software) or Premium (HSM) tiers.

4. Security Solutions Part 2 — Defender for Cloud & Sentinel

  • Defender for Cloud (CNAPP): Three pillars — CSPM (posture management, Secure Score, MCSB compliance, foundational features free), CWPP (per-workload Defender plans for servers, containers, databases, storage), DevSecOps (GitHub/Azure DevOps integration, IaC scanning, PR annotation remediation).
  • MCSB: Microsoft Cloud Security Benchmark — the default security initiative. Defines individual policy rules grouped into initiatives. Non-compliant resources generate security recommendations with point values toward the Secure Score.
  • Secure Score: Single snapshot of overall risk. Recommendations grouped into security controls. Fixing high-priority issues increases the score. CSPM plan adds advanced posture management.
  • Microsoft Sentinel: Cloud-native SIEM+SOAR. Four functions: Collect (built-in/custom connectors, Syslog, REST APIs, ASIM normalization), Detect (analytics rules, MITRE ATT&CK mapping, threat intelligence), Investigate (incidents as case files, KQL hunting, notebooks), Respond (automation rules, playbooks via Azure Logic Apps for account disable, traffic block, ticket creation).
  • Sentinel + Copilot: Standalone plugin + embedded experience in Defender portal. Natural language to KQL query generation, incident summarization, guided investigation flows with built-in prompt books.
  • MITRE ATT&CK: Public knowledge base of attacker tactics and techniques. Sentinel maps all analytics rules and detections to this framework for organized threat understanding.

5. Security Solutions Part 3 — Defender XDR

  • Defender XDR: Correlates signals across identities, devices, email, cloud apps, and infrastructure into unified attack stories. Automatic alert correlation enriches with threat intelligence, reducing investigation time.
  • Defender for Office 365: Safe attachments (detonation chamber), safe links, anti-phishing/anti-malware. Zero-hour auto-purge (ZAP) auto-removes malicious messages after delivery. Investigation: Explorer, Audit Log Search, Message Trace.
  • Defender for Endpoint: Behavioral sensors + cloud analytics + Microsoft Threat Intelligence. Next-gen AV, automated investigation and response across laptops, desktops, servers.
  • Defender for Cloud Apps: Cloud Discovery against 37,000+ app catalog (shadow IT detection). Risk assessment scores (security, compliance, legal). Activity logs, policy management. SSPM recommendations. Detects anomalous user behavior and risky OAuth permissions.
  • Defender for Identity: Lightweight sensors on AD domain controllers. Detects privilege escalation, lateral movement, abnormal sign-ins. Remediation: disable accounts, force password resets from Defender portal.
  • Defender Vulnerability Management: Continuous asset discovery across Windows, macOS, Linux, mobile, network. Risk-based prioritization with threat intelligence. Built-in remediation tracking from discovery to resolution.
  • Defender Threat Intelligence: Threat Analytics (active campaigns), Intel Explorer (IoCs, CVEs, keywords search), Projects (organize indicators of compromise). Integrates with Security Copilot for natural language threat summarization.
  • Defender Portal: Unified security operations — exposure management (attack surface map), incidents/alerts, advanced hunting (KQL), threat intelligence, assets (devices, identities, apps), Secure Score, configuration management.

6. Microsoft Priva & Microsoft Purview

  • Service Trust Portal: servicetrust.microsoft.com — audit reports, certifications, standards, white papers. Public access; sensitive docs require sign-in + NDA. Organized by certifications, reports, regional/industry materials, tenant-specific resources.
  • Privacy Principles: Control (you own your data), Transparency (clear collection documentation), Security (encryption at rest and in transit), Strong legal protections (Microsoft validates government requests), No content-based targeting (no advertising use), Benefit to customer (data improves reliability).
  • Microsoft Priva: Privacy Risk Management (overexposure, risky transfers, over-retention), Subject Rights Requests (automated access/deletion workflows), Consent Management (centralized consumer consent), Tracker Scanning (website tracking detection), Privacy Assessments (auto-evaluate data processing).
  • Purview Information Protection: Sensitive info types (pattern-based: credit cards, passports), EDM classifiers (exact data match), trainable classifiers (ML for contracts/invoices). Content Explorer (where labeled data lives), Activity Explorer (user actions over time).
  • Sensitivity Labels: Persistent, clear-text metadata traveling with content. Can encrypt, watermark, auto-classify. Label policies control visibility, set defaults, require justification for downgrade, enforce mandatory labeling. Container labels for SharePoint sites/M365 groups.
  • DLP: Real-time detection across Exchange, SharePoint, OneDrive, Teams, endpoints, cloud apps, Power BI. Policy tips → block with/without override. Endpoint DLP covers USB, printing, unapproved apps.
  • Insider Risk Management: Policies → risk indicators → alerts → triage → cases → remediation. Adaptive Protection uses ML to assess user risk and auto-adjust DLP/retention/CA controls accordingly.
  • Audit: Standard (90-day retention, default) vs Premium (1-year, custom retention policies, higher bandwidth API). Searchable via UI, CLI, API. Security Copilot actions logged through Purview Audit.
  • eDiscovery: Content Search (basic keyword), Standard (cases + legal holds), Premium (analytics + custodian management + full workflow). Copilot integration for review set summarization and natural language to search query.
  • Compliance Manager: Prebuilt assessments (ISO 27001, GDPR). Improvement actions with point values. Compliance Score = shared responsibility view (Microsoft-managed + customer-managed). Actions classified as mandatory/discretionary and preventative/detective/corrective.
  • Data Lifecycle Management: Retention labels (item-level, travel with content, disposition review) vs retention policies (broad-level, containers inherit). Records management: records (no edit/delete, activity logged, proof of disposition) and regulatory records (label cannot be removed, retention cannot be shortened even by admins).
  • Purview Data Catalog: Business domains (sales, finance), data products, glossary terms, critical data elements. Federated governance (data owners + stewards curate, central data office sets policy). Self-service data access, search/browse, health management, data quality.

Key Concepts

Security & Identity Fundamentals

  • Shared Responsibility: Pizza analogy — on-prem = homemade, IaaS = pizza base, PaaS = partially prepared, SaaS = delivered. Customer ALWAYS retains data, devices, identities regardless of model.
  • Defense in Depth: Seven layers — Physical → Identity → Perimeter → Network → Compute → Application → Data. Multiple overlapping controls prevent single points of failure.
  • Zero Trust: Six pillars (Identities, Devices, Apps, Data, Infrastructure, Networks) + three principles (verify explicitly, least privilege via JEA/JIT, assume breach).
  • Encryption: Symmetric (same key, bulk data) vs Asymmetric (public/private pair, TLS/digital signatures). Protects data at rest, in transit, and in use.
  • Hashing + Salt: One-way, deterministic, fixed-length. Salt = per-user random value before hashing to defeat rainbow tables. Passwords stored as salted hashes.
  • GRC: Governance (policies, oversight), Risk (identify/mitigate threats), Compliance (follow laws like GDPR, HIPAA, ISO 27001). Data residency (geographic), sovereignty (legal), privacy (usage).

Entra ID & Access Management

  • Four Pillars of Identity: Administration (provision), Authentication (prove), Authorization (allow), Audit (track). All four must work together.
  • Hybrid Identity: Entra Connect (on-prem sync engine) vs Entra Cloud Sync (cloud-based, future direction). Auth options: PHS (recommended), PTA (on-prem validation), or Federation (AD FS).
  • MFA Factors: Knowledge (password/PIN), Possession (phone/token/FIDO2), Inherence (biometric). Passwordless methods: Windows Hello, Authenticator, FIDO2 passkeys, CBA.
  • Conditional Access: If-then engine — signals (user group, location, device, risk, app) → controls (block, grant MFA, require compliant device, session controls like sign-in frequency).
  • Global Secure Access: Entra Internet Access (SaaS/web security) + Entra Private Access (ZTNA replaces VPN). Identity-driven SSE — routes traffic through Entra edge.
  • PIM: Just-in-time role elevation — eligible (no standing access), activate with MFA + justification + approval, time-bound (1-8 hours), fully audited.
  • Identity Protection: User risk (leaked credentials on dark web) + Sign-in risk (atypical travel, anonymous IP, unfamiliar properties). Feeds into Conditional Access for automated remediation.

Microsoft Security Solutions

  • Security Copilot: AI-powered analysis — standalone mode (dedicated portal) + embedded mode (inside Sentinel, Defender, Entra). Key terms: Session, Prompt, Plugin, Workspace, Orchestrator (composes capabilities), Agent (autonomous tasks).
  • Azure Infra Security: DDoS Protection (Network/IP tiers), Azure Firewall (L4-7 stateful, TLS inspection), WAF on Front Door (global) or App Gateway (regional), NSGs (priority 100-4096), Azure Bastion (no public IP RDP/SSH), Key Vault (secrets, keys, certs).
  • Defender for Cloud: Three pillars — CSPM (Secure Score via MCSB), CWPP (per-workload Defender plans), DevSecOps (GitHub/Azure DevOps IaC scanning, PR remediation).
  • Microsoft Sentinel: Four functions — Collect (connectors + ASIM normalization), Detect (analytics rules + MITRE ATT&CK), Investigate (incidents + KQL hunting), Respond (playbooks via Logic Apps).
  • Defender XDR: Office 365 (Safe Attachments/Links, ZAP), Endpoint (EDR + AIR + vulnerability mgmt), Cloud Apps (shadow IT via 37k app catalog), Identity (on-prem AD sensors), Threat Intelligence (Intel Explorer, Projects), unified in Defender portal.

Compliance & Privacy

  • Service Trust Portal: servicetrust.microsoft.com — audit reports, ISO/SOC/PCI certifications, compliance whitepapers. Privacy principles: Control, Transparency, Security, Legal protections, No content-based targeting, Benefit to customer.
  • Microsoft Priva: Privacy Risk Management, Subject Rights Requests (automated GDPR access/deletion), Consent Management, Tracker Scanning.
  • Sensitivity Labels: Persistent clear-text metadata — encrypt, watermark, auto-classify via SITs or trainable classifiers. Travel with content. Container labels for SharePoint/M365 groups.
  • DLP: Real-time protection across M365, endpoints, cloud apps. Policy tips → block with/without override. Insider Risk Management (alerts → cases → remediation) + Adaptive Protection (ML adjusts controls by risk level).
  • Audit: Standard (90-180 day retention) vs Premium (1-year+, custom policies, higher bandwidth API). eDiscovery: Content Search < Standard < Premium (custodians, analytics, holds).
  • Compliance Manager: Prebuilt assessments (ISO, GDPR), improvement actions with point values, shared responsibility compliance score. Retention labels (item-level, travel with content) vs policies (container-level). Regulatory records = strongest protection (irremovable label).
  • Purview Data Catalog: Business domains, data products, glossary terms, CDEs. Federated governance — central standards + decentralized ownership. Data quality rules + health management.

SC-900 Key Pointers

Quick Reference — All Domains

Module: SC-900 Key Pointers Quick Reference

25 Categories | Exam Review

1. Exam Basics

  • Passing score is 700 out of 1000, with 40-60 questions to be completed in 60 minutes.
  • Question formats include multiple-choice, multi-select, drag-and-drop, and scenario-based questions.
  • Four domains: Security/Compliance/Identity Concepts (10-15%), Entra Capabilities (25-30%), Security Solutions (35-40%), and Compliance Solutions (20-25%).

2. Shared Responsibility Model

  • On-premises: the customer manages and secures the entire technology stack from physical hardware to data.
  • IaaS: the customer manages from the operating system upward; the provider handles physical infrastructure, hosts, and networking hardware.
  • PaaS: the customer manages data, identities, and devices; the provider handles the operating system and runtime environment.
  • SaaS: the customer manages only identities and devices; the provider handles the application, OS, network, and infrastructure.
  • The customer always retains responsibility for identities, devices, and data regardless of the service model.
  • AI shared responsibility extends the model across three layers: AI platform (provider secures infrastructure and foundation models), AI application (customer secures prompts, data, and app logic), and AI usage (customer governs acceptable use and mitigates prompt injection risks).

3. Defense in Depth

  • Seven layers (outermost → innermost): Physical (datacenter access, biometrics), Identity (MFA, authN/Z), Perimeter (DDoS protection, firewall), Network (NSGs, network segmentation), Compute (antimalware, patch management, vulnerability scanning), Application (WAF, input validation, secure coding), Data (encryption at rest/transit, access controls, DLP).
  • Each layer provides independent protection — if one layer is breached, the next layer still blocks the attacker. No single point of failure for security.
  • Data is the innermost and most critical layer because it is the ultimate target of most attacks. Every other layer exists to protect it.
  • The exam expects you to identify which layer a specific control belongs to (e.g., "MFA" = Identity layer, "WAF" = Application layer).

4. CIA Triad

  • Confidentiality: data is accessible only to authorized parties. Enforced through encryption (at rest and in transit), access controls (RBAC, Conditional Access), and the principle of least privilege.
  • Integrity: data has not been tampered with. Enforced through hashing (verify file integrity), digital signatures (prove origin + integrity), and audit logs (detect unauthorized changes).
  • Availability: services are accessible when needed. Enforced through redundancy (availability zones), DDoS protection, backups, and disaster recovery planning.
  • All three must be balanced — focusing on one at the expense of others creates risk. For example, maximum encryption (confidentiality) without backup (availability) means data loss if keys are lost.
  • Exam tip: scenario questions often ask which element of the triad is most impacted by a specific event (e.g., ransomware = availability, data breach = confidentiality).

5. Zero Trust

  • Three guiding principles: Verify explicitly (always authenticate and authorize based on ALL available signals — identity, device, location, risk), Use least privilege access (JEA/JIT — grant minimum permissions needed, time-bound elevation), Assume breach (design for breach — segment networks, encrypt end-to-end, limit blast radius, micro-perimeters).
  • Seven pillars: Identities, Devices, Applications, Data, Infrastructure, Networks, and Visibility (telemetry, analytics, and automation). Each pillar is evaluated continuously, not just at the perimeter.
  • Identity is the primary security perimeter in cloud environments — the traditional network perimeter (firewall/VPN) is no longer sufficient because users access resources from anywhere on any device.
  • Zero Trust is a guiding philosophy, not a specific product. Microsoft implements it through Entra ID (Conditional Access, PIM), Defender XDR, Intune, and Microsoft Purview.
  • Exam tip: Zero Trust questions test whether you understand that trust is NEVER assumed based on network location — a user inside the corporate network must be verified just as strictly as one connecting from a coffee shop.

6. Encryption and Hashing

  • Symmetric encryption uses the same key to encrypt and decrypt; the main challenge is secure key distribution.
  • Asymmetric encryption uses a public/private key pair; data encrypted with the public key can only be decrypted with the private key.
  • Digital signatures are created by encrypting a hash with the sender's private key, proving both integrity and authenticity.
  • Hashing is a one-way function that produces a fixed-length output, commonly used for password storage and integrity verification.
  • Salting adds a unique random value to each password before hashing to prevent rainbow table attacks.
  • Azure Key Vault stores secrets (read/write access), keys (no export, cryptographic operations performed inside the vault), and certificates (lifecycle management).

7. GRC (Governance, Risk, Compliance)

  • Governance defines the rules, practices, and processes for organizational direction and control.
  • Risk management identifies, assesses, and responds to internal and external threats.
  • Compliance is the adherence to laws, regulations, and standards applicable to the organization.
  • Data residency = where data physically lives (geography). Data sovereignty = whose laws apply (legal). Data privacy = how data is handled (rights). All three overlap but address different concerns.

8. Identity Fundamentals

  • Identity types include user (human), service principal (application), managed identity (Azure-managed), device, workload, and agent.
  • The four pillars of identity are Administration, Authentication, Authorization, and Audit.
  • Entra ID is the cloud-based identity provider (formerly Azure AD) that speaks OAuth 2.0, OIDC, and SAML.
  • AD DS is the on-premises directory service using Kerberos and NTLM with a hierarchical structure based on organizational units.
  • SSO allows a user to authenticate once and access all trusted services without re-entering credentials.
  • Federation establishes trust between identity providers to enable cross-organizational access using SAML, OAuth 2.0, or OpenID Connect.
  • Hybrid identity connects on-premises AD with Entra ID using Cloud Sync (cloud engine, future direction) or Entra Connect (on-premises engine).
  • Password Hash Sync synchronizes a hash of the user's password from AD DS to Entra ID, not the actual password. Pass-through Authentication validates against on-prem AD in real-time.
  • B2B Collaboration invites external users as guests who authenticate with their own identity provider. B2B Direct Connect enables mutual trust for Teams shared channels without guest accounts.
  • Entra External ID (B2C/CIAM) provides customer-facing identity with self-service registration and social identity login (Google, Facebook, Apple).
  • Entra Agent ID provides first-class identity for AI agents with dedicated governance, lifecycle, and audit trail.

9. Authentication and MFA

  • Three MFA factor categories: something you know (password), something you have (phone or key), and something you are (biometrics).
  • Passwordless methods include Microsoft Authenticator, FIDO2 passkeys, Windows Hello for Business, and Certificate-Based Authentication (CBA).
  • Passkeys (FIDO2) are phishing-resistant and require device proximity such as Bluetooth between devices.
  • Security defaults provide baseline MFA enforcement for all users when Conditional Access is not available.
  • Password protection uses a global banned list and a custom banned list, enforceable on both Entra ID and on-premises AD DS.
  • SSPR (Self-Service Password Reset) lets users reset their own passwords after verifying identity, reducing help desk load. Requires P1 licensing.
  • Temporary Access Pass (TAP) is a time-limited passcode issued by admins for onboarding new users or recovering access to register passwordless methods.

10. Conditional Access & Authentication Strengths

  • Conditional Access is Microsoft's Zero Trust policy engine — evaluates signals AFTER first-factor authentication and applies access controls based on if-then logic.
  • Policy Assignments (the "if"): users/groups (include + exclude), target resources (cloud apps, user actions), conditions (device platform, location/IP ranges, client app, sign-in risk). All conditions are logically ANDed — all must match for the policy to apply.
  • Access Controls (the "then"): Grant (block, require MFA, require compliant/hybrid joined device, require approved client app, require app protection policy, require password change, require terms of use) or Session (app-enforced restrictions, sign-in frequency, persistent browser session, Global Secure Access controls).
  • Grant control logic: Require all selected controls (AND — user must satisfy every control) vs Require one of the selected controls (OR — any one is enough). This AND vs OR distinction is a common exam question.
  • Authentication Strengths specify acceptable MFA method combinations: MFA (any factor), Passwordless MFA (passwordless methods only), or Phishing-Resistant MFA (FIDO2 passkeys, CBA, Windows Hello — must be hardware-bound).
  • Requires Entra ID P1 licensing. Risk-based policies (sign-in risk, user risk) require P2.

11. PIM & Access Reviews

  • PIM provides just-in-time elevation where users are eligible by default and activate privileged roles on demand for a defined time window with MFA and justification. Three role types: Entra roles, Azure resources, and groups.
  • Activation requires approval (one or two approvers), a justification, and MFA. Activations are time-bound and fully audited with a history trail.
