  • Access reviews are periodic checks that confirm whether users still need their group, application, or role access. Results are automatically applied (remove access for denied users) or manually reviewed.
  • Multi-stage reviews allow up to three sequential reviewers (e.g., manager → resource owner → compliance officer).

12. RBAC & Entra Roles

  • RBAC assigns permissions through a role assignment: a role (set of permissions) plus an identity (user, group, service principal) plus a scope (management group, subscription, resource group, resource).
  • Built-in Entra roles: Global Administrator (full access), User Administrator, Security Administrator, Billing Administrator, Exchange Admin, Intune Admin, and many service-specific roles.
  • Custom roles: collections of chosen permissions assigned at org-wide or specific-object scope (a single app or admin unit). Requires P1/P2 licensing.
  • Administrative Units scope admin permissions to specific objects — useful for regional or departmental admins.
  • Key distinction: Entra RBAC controls identity resources (users, groups, apps); Azure RBAC controls infrastructure resources (VMs, storage, networking).
  • Least privilege principle: always assign the minimum role needed. Global Admin should be reserved for break-glass scenarios only.

13. Identity Protection

  • Identity Protection evaluates user risk (aggregate identity risk over time) and sign-in risk (per-event risk based on real-time signals) to detect compromised identities.
  • Risk types: leaked credentials, anonymous IP, atypical travel, malicious IP, unfamiliar sign-in properties, password spray, token replay, and more.
  • Automated remediation policies respond to risk levels: require MFA for medium+ risk, require password change for high user risk, or block access for high sign-in risk.
  • Investigation: risk detections are grouped into risky users and risky sign-ins reports. Dismiss or confirm compromise to provide feedback for the ML model.
  • Requires Entra ID P2 licensing (included in M365 E5).

14. Identity Governance

  • Joiner/Mover/Leaver lifecycle automation uses lifecycle workflows triggered by start and end dates — automatically provision, update, or deprovision access.
  • Entitlement Management provides access packages bundling groups, apps, and SharePoint sites with policies for self-service requests, approvals (one or two stages), and time-bound access with expiration.
  • Verified ID uses decentralized identity with verifiable credentials based on open standards (W3C VC, DID). Three parties: issuer (trusted authority), holder (user wallet), and verifier (relying party).
  • Permissions Management discovers and remediates excessive permissions across Azure, AWS, and GCP with the Permission Creep Index (PCI).
  • Entra Private Access is a Zero Trust VPN replacement that redirects private network traffic through the Entra edge.
  • Entra Internet Access secures outbound internet traffic with FQDN and category filtering.
  • Entra Suite combines P1 and P2 features with Private Access, Internet Access, Governance, and Identity Protection.

15. Azure Network Security

  • DDoS Protection Basic is free and protects against high-volume attacks only; Standard offers Network or IP tiers with ML-tuned, custom policies.
  • Azure Firewall operates at Layer 4 (network) and Layer 7 (application) with TLS inspection and threat intelligence filtering.
  • WAF protects against OWASP top exploits using the Core Rule Set and is deployed on Front Door (global) or Application Gateway (regional).
  • Virtual Networks provide regional isolation and cannot communicate by default; peering enables connectivity between vNets.
  • NSGs define rules by source/destination IP, port, and protocol and are typically assigned to subnets.
  • Virtual Network Manager Security Admin Rules are processed before NSGs; Always Allow bypasses NSG rules.
  • Azure Bastion is a managed jump box for RDP and SSH access to VMs without exposing public IPs.

16. Security Copilot

  • AI-powered security analysis tool built on Azure OpenAI Services with a security-specific model, not just generic GPT-4.
  • Standalone mode uses a dedicated Copilot portal for cross-product investigations; embedded mode integrates directly inside Sentinel, Defender, Entra, Purview, and Intune.
  • Key terminology: Session (conversation context), Prompt (natural language instruction), Plugin (data source connector), Workspace (isolated environment), Orchestrator (composes capabilities), Agent (autonomous assistant).
  • Licensed via Security Compute Units (SCUs) billed per hour, or included with M365 E5/E7 starting 2025 via zero-click activation.
  • Customer data is not used to train foundation AI models. Data remains within the organization's tenant.

17. Defender for Cloud

  • Cloud-native application protection platform (CNAPP) with three pillars: CSPM (posture management), CWPP (workload protection), and DevSecOps (shift-left security).
  • Foundational CSPM is free for all Azure subscriptions and provides Secure Score, MCSB compliance assessment, and security recommendations.
  • Secure Score reflects overall security posture; each recommendation has a point value based on severity. Fixing high-priority issues increases the score most.
  • CWPP provides per-workload Defender plans: Servers, Storage, Databases, Containers, Key Vault, and AI Services.
  • DevSecOps integrates security into CI/CD pipelines via Defender for DevOps with code scanning, secrets detection, and IaC analysis.
  • Attack Path Analysis models how attackers could chain multiple vulnerabilities to reach high-value resources.

18. Microsoft Sentinel

  • Cloud-native SIEM (collect, detect, investigate) and SOAR (automated response with playbooks) built on a Log Analytics workspace.
  • Collect: 350+ built-in data connectors plus custom API/Syslog/CEF connectors. ASIM normalizes data from different sources into a common schema.
  • Detect: Analytics rules (scheduled queries, ML behavioral analytics, Fusion correlation engine, threat intelligence matching) generate alerts grouped into incidents. MITRE ATT&CK maps every detection rule.
  • Investigate: Incidents as case files with graph, timeline, and entity pages. KQL hunting queries proactively search for suspicious activity. Notebooks enable advanced data science investigations.
  • Respond: Automation rules execute playbooks (Azure Logic Apps workflows) for automated remediation. Content Hub provides packaged solutions bundling connectors, workbooks, and rules.
  • Sentinel Data Lake provides cost-effective long-term storage in open format (Parquet/JSON) for up to 12 years.

19. Defender XDR

  • Unified pre- and post-breach defense suite coordinating detection, prevention, investigation, and response across endpoints, identities, email, and cloud apps.
  • Combined incidents queue automatically correlates related alerts from all Defender products into a single incident showing the entire attack story.
  • Automatic attack disruption correlates signals to detect active attacks and contain them in real-time by isolating devices, disabling accounts, or blocking connections.
  • Defender for Office 365: Safe Attachments (detonation chamber), Safe Links (time-of-click URL scanning), anti-phishing, and Zero-Hour Auto-Purge (ZAP). Plan 1 (protection) vs Plan 2 (investigation, hunting, simulation).
  • Defender for Endpoint: Unified EPP + EDR with attack surface reduction, next-gen AV, automated investigation and remediation (AIR), and vulnerability management.
  • Defender for Identity: Lightweight sensors on AD domain controllers detecting lateral movement, privilege escalation, and domain dominance attacks.
  • Defender for Cloud Apps: CASB with Cloud Discovery against 37,000+ app catalog, shadow IT detection, SSPM, and app governance.
  • The Defender portal provides a unified SOC combining XDR incidents, SIEM (Sentinel), posture management, threat intelligence, and exposure management.

20. Compliance Principles

  • Microsoft's six privacy principles: Control (you own your data), Transparency (clear data practices), Security (encryption at rest/transit), Legal Protections (challenge government requests), No Content-Based Targeting (don't use customer content for ads), Benefit to Customer (use data only to improve services).
  • Service Trust Portal (servicetrust.microsoft.com): central hub for compliance documentation — audit reports (SOC, ISO, FedRAMP), certifications, data protection whitepapers, and regional/industry-specific compliance resources.
  • My Library in STP lets you save, bookmark, and track relevant documents with email notifications when documents are updated or expire.
  • Compliance offerings are organized by service (Azure, M365, Dynamics) and by industry/region (GDPR, HIPAA, NIST, PCI DSS, ISO 27001, SOC 2).

21. Microsoft Priva

  • Privacy Risk Management discovers where private data lives and helps limit its transfer across boundaries.
  • Subject Rights Requests handle the complete workflow for individuals requesting access to or deletion of their personal data.
  • Consent Management tracks and manages consumer consent across services.
  • Tracker Scanning finds web tracking technologies on your sites.

22. Microsoft Purview

  • Purview is built on three pillars: Governance, Compliance, and Data Security.
  • Compliance Manager tracks a compliance score, assessments, and improvement actions assigned to individuals.
  • The data lifecycle follows five steps: Know, Classify, Protect, Prevent, and Govern.
  • Sensitivity labels provide classification plus actions (watermark, encryption, access controls) and are stored as clear-text metadata with a single label per item.
  • Retention policies keep or delete data based on defined requirements and time periods. Retention labels apply at item level and travel with content.
  • Records management restricts activities on labeled records, logs all actions, and provides proof of disposition. Regulatory records are the strongest protection (label cannot be removed).
  • DLP prevents data loss based on sensitivity labels and sensitive information types across M365, endpoints, and cloud apps.
  • Insider Risk Management uses policies to generate alerts that are triaged into cases for investigation.
  • Adaptive Protection uses ML to assess user risk level and dynamically adjusts DLP, retention, and Conditional Access policies for that user.
  • Communication Compliance detects code of conduct violations in email, Teams, Viva Engage, and Copilot interactions using pre-built templates and ML classifiers.
  • Information Barriers restrict communication between segments for compliance (e.g., trading vs advisory departments).
  • eDiscovery tiers: Content Search (basic) < Standard (cases and legal holds) < Premium (full end-to-end workflow with custodians, analytics, and redactions).
  • Audit Standard retains logs for 90 days; Audit Premium retains logs for 1 year and provides a higher-bandwidth API with custom retention policies.

23. Data Governance

  • Federated governance model: centralized safety and standards with decentralized ownership across business domains to reduce bottlenecks.
  • Data roles: data consumers (find and use data), data owners (register and manage assets), data stewards (ensure quality and policies), central data office (set governance policies).
  • Microsoft Purview Data Map scans and catalogs data sources from Azure, M365, and on-premises. Automatically discovers assets, classifies sensitive information, and maps lineage.
  • Unified Catalog builds on Data Map metadata to provide a business-friendly view for discovering and understanding data assets.
  • Governance Domains organize data by business concept (Marketing, Finance, Sales). Data Products are named, owned data assets serving a specific use case.
  • Glossary Terms provide business-language definitions for consistent understanding. Critical Data Elements (CDEs) group important information with quality rules and access policies.
  • Data Quality evaluates data using no-code rules and AI-generated rules. Scores published at asset, product, and domain levels.

24. DSPM & Data Security Investigations

  • DSPM (Data Security Posture Management) provides a unified view of data security risks across M365, Azure, Fabric, and non-Microsoft environments (GCP, Snowflake, Databricks via partner integrations).
  • AI observability dashboards monitor AI-related data risks — Copilot interactions, sensitive data in prompts, and agent activities across the data estate.
  • Data risk assessments identify where sensitive data lives, who has access, and whether it is overexposed — with posture metrics and prioritized remediation recommendations.
  • Data Security Investigations uses vector search (semantic similarity meaning, not keyword matching), auto-categorization, and deep examination for triaging data security incidents.
  • Actions: soft purge (remove from user view but retain for recovery) or hard purge (permanent deletion) of sensitive content in investigation results.

25. Licensing Quick Reference

  • Conditional Access policies require Entra ID P1. Risk-based Conditional Access (sign-in/user risk) requires P2.
  • PIM, Identity Protection, and Access Reviews require Entra ID P2 (included in M365 E5).
  • Defender for Office 365 Plan 1 (Safe Attachments/Links) is in E3 and Business Premium. Plan 2 (AIR, Threat Explorer, simulation training) requires E5.
  • Defender for Endpoint P2 (advanced EDR, AIR, vulnerability management) requires E5 or Defender Suite.
  • Defender for Identity and Defender for Cloud Apps (CASB) require E5 or Defender Suite.
  • Microsoft Sentinel is pay-as-you-go Azure billing (not included in M365 SKUs), but security alerts from Defender are free ingestion.
  • Security Copilot is included with M365 E5/E7 starting 2025, or requires standalone SCU provisioning.
  • Auto-labeling, DLP for Teams/Endpoints, Insider Risk Management, Communication Compliance, eDiscovery Premium, Audit Premium, and Priva require E5 or Purview Suite.
  • M365 E5 bundles deliver the best value: Entra P2 + full Defender XDR + full Purview Suite + Security Copilot.

Section Summary

Exam Basics

  • Passing score 700/1000, 40–60 questions, 60 minutes. Four domains: Security/Compliance/Identity Concepts (10–15%), Entra Capabilities (25–30%), Security Solutions (35–40%), Compliance Solutions (20–25%). Formats: multiple-choice, multi-select, drag-and-drop, scenario-based

1. Security, Compliance & Identity Concepts

  • Shared Responsibility: Customer manages everything on-prem; IaaS shifts OS+upward to customer; PaaS shifts runtime+up; SaaS leaves only identities/devices/data with customer. Customer ALWAYS retains identities, devices, data regardless of model. AI shared responsibility extends across three layers: AI platform (provider secures infrastructure/models), AI application (customer secures prompts/data/logic), AI usage (customer governs acceptable use and mitigates prompt injection)
  • Defense in Depth: Seven layers (Physical → Identity → Perimeter → Network → Compute → Application → Data) — each layer independent, failure of one does not expose the next. Data is the innermost/most critical layer
  • CIA Triad: Confidentiality (encryption + access controls), Integrity (hashing + digital signatures to detect tampering), Availability (redundancy + DDoS protection + backups)
  • Zero Trust: Three principles — Verify explicitly (check identity, device, location, behavior), Least privilege (JEA/JIT), Assume breach (segment, limit blast radius). Seven pillars: Identities, Devices, Applications, Data, Infrastructure, Networks, Visibility. Identity is the primary security perimeter in the cloud
  • Encryption & Hashing: Symmetric (same key encrypts/decrypts, key distribution challenge). Asymmetric (public/private pair — data encrypted with public key decrypted only by private key). Digital signatures (encrypt hash with sender's private key = integrity + authenticity). Hashing (one-way, fixed-length, for passwords/integrity). Salting (per-user random value before hashing defeats rainbow tables). Azure Key Vault stores secrets (read/write), keys (crypto inside vault, no export), certificates (TLS lifecycle)
  • GRC: Governance (policies/oversight), Risk (identify/assess/respond), Compliance (adhere to laws). Data residency (geographic location of data), data sovereignty (which country's laws apply), data privacy (how data is collected/used/shared). All three overlap but address different concerns
  • Identity Fundamentals: Identity types — user, service principal, managed identity, device, workload, agent. Four pillars: Administration, Authentication, Authorization, Audit. Entra ID = cloud IdP (OAuth 2.0, OIDC, SAML). AD DS = on-prem directory (Kerberos, NTLM, OUs). SSO = authenticate once, access all trusted services. Federation = trust between IdPs for cross-org access. Hybrid sync via Cloud Sync or Entra Connect. PHS syncs hash-of-hash, not the actual password. B2B Collaboration (guests authenticate with home org). B2B Direct Connect (mutual trust for Teams shared channels). External ID (CIAM for consumer apps). Agent ID (first-class identity for AI agents)
  • Authentication & MFA: Three factor categories — knowledge (password), possession (phone/key), inherence (biometrics). Passwordless: Microsoft Authenticator, FIDO2 passkeys (phishing-resistant, requires Bluetooth proximity), Windows Hello for Business, Certificate-Based Authentication. Security defaults = baseline MFA when no Conditional Access. Password Protection = global banned list (always-on) + custom banned list (org-specific), enforced in Entra ID and on-prem AD DS. SSPR (self-service password reset) reduces help desk load. Temporary Access Pass (TAP) for onboarding and recovery
  • Authorization & Access: Conditional Access = if-then engine (signals: user, location, device, risk → controls: MFA, block, compliant device). Grant control logic: Require all selected controls (AND) or Require one of the selected controls (OR). Authentication Strengths specify acceptable MFA combinations (MFA, Passwordless MFA, Phishing-Resistant MFA). RBAC = role (permission set) + identity + scope. PIM = just-in-time elevation (eligible by default, activate on demand for time-bound window with approval). Access reviews = periodic recertification of group/app/role access
  • Identity Governance: Joiner/Mover/Leaver lifecycle workflows (triggered by start/end dates). Identity Protection (user risk + sign-in risk for compromised identity detection). Entitlement Management (access packages bundling groups/apps/sites with policies for self-service requests and approvals). Verified ID (decentralized identity with verifiable credentials, issuer/holder/verifier model). Permissions Management (discover/remediate across Azure, AWS, GCP). Entra Private Access (Zero Trust VPN replacement). Entra Internet Access (FQDN/category filtering for outbound traffic). Entra Suite = P1+P2 + Private Access + Internet Access + Governance + Identity Protection

2. Microsoft Entra (25–30% of exam)

  • Entra ID: Core cloud IAM for authentication, SSO, policy enforcement. Every M365/Azure/Dynamics tenant gets one automatically. Tenant = directory representing one organization. Identity types: human (employees/guests), workload (service principals/managed identities), device, agent
  • Hybrid Identity: Cloud Sync (cloud-based, future direction) or Entra Connect (on-prem sync engine). Auth options: Password Hash Sync (recommended, enables leaked credential detection), Pass-through Authentication (on-prem agent validates), Federation (AD FS or third-party IdP). Seamless SSO for domain-joined devices on corporate network
  • External Identities: B2B Collaboration (share apps with guests who authenticate using their home org — no new credentials). B2B direct connect (mutual trust for Teams shared channels). External ID (CIAM for consumer-facing apps with self-service registration, social identity login)
  • Authentication Methods: Passwords, phone (SMS/voice/OATH tokens), passwordless (Windows Hello, Authenticator, FIDO2, certificate-based). MFA requires 2+ categories. Security defaults enforced for all users without P1/P2. SSPR with registration, notifications, writeback, recovery. Password Protection extends to on-prem AD via proxy
  • Conditional Access: If-then — assignments (user/group, location, device platform, risk, client app) → access controls (block, grant with MFA/ compliant device/ hybrid join, session controls like sign-in frequency and app enforced restrictions). Session policies for Global Secure Access with FQDN filtering and web content filtering
  • Global Secure Access: SSE combining Entra Internet Access (SaaS/web security, tenant restrictions, content filtering) + Entra Private Access (VPN replacement for private apps). Lightweight client on devices routes traffic through Entra edge. Microsoft Entra Internet Access (acquired from Cato Networks) + Microsoft Entra Private Access
  • RBAC: Built-in roles (Global Admin, User Admin, Security Admin, Billing Admin, Exchange Admin, etc.) + custom roles. Three categories: Global Admin roles (broad), Delegated Admin roles (specific), least privilege always. Entra RBAC controls identity resources; Azure RBAC controls infrastructure
  • Identity Governance: Lifecycle workflows (joiner/mover/leaver with triggers). Access reviews (periodic recertification, multi-stage up to 3 reviewers). Entitlement Management (access packages with catalogs, approvals, assignments). PIM (JIT elevation with MFA + justification + approval + time-bound activation, fully audited). Identity Protection (user risk + sign-in risk, automated remediation: MFA, password reset, block). Verified ID (decentralized identity with issuers/verifiers/holders, Face Check). Security Copilot in Entra (alert summarization, Triage Agent)
  • Agent ID: New identity type for AI agents — dedicated governance, lifecycle, and audit trail for autonomous AI agent actions

3. Security Solutions (35–40% of exam)

  • Azure Network Security: DDoS Protection Basic (free, high-volume only) vs Standard (Network/IP tiers, ML-tuned custom policies, mitigation reports/alerts). Azure Firewall (L4+L7, TLS inspection, threat intelligence). WAF (OWASP CRS, deployed on Front Door global or App Gateway regional). vNets (regional isolation, peering for connectivity). NSGs (rules by IP/port/protocol, assigned to subnets). Virtual Network Manager Security Admin Rules (processed before NSGs). Azure Bastion (managed RDP/SSH jump box, no public IPs)
  • Defender for Cloud: CNAPP with four pillars — CSPM (secure score, MCSB, regulatory compliance), CWPP (Defender plans for servers/containers/databases), DevSecOps (shift left), and Agentless machine scanning. Foundational CSPM is free; workload protection requires per-resource Defender plans. Connecting non-Azure via connectors (AWS/GCP) or Azure Arc (on-prem servers). Security policies = MCSB initiatives (built-in) or custom
  • Microsoft Sentinel: Cloud-native SIEM (collect/detect/investigate across enterprise) + SOAR (automated response with playbooks). Built on Log Analytics workspace. Connects Microsoft and third-party data sources. AI/ML for correlation. Investigation graph. Sentinel graph (knowledge graph for SOC). Security Copilot for Microsoft Defender (unified SOC). MCP integration with GitHub, ServiceNow. Scheduled/near-real-time analytics rules
  • Security Copilot: AI assistant for security professionals — embedded (inside Defender/Sentinel/Purview portals) and immersive (standalone prompt portal). Requires SCUs. Capabilities: incident summarization, script analysis, reverse engineering, KQL generation for Sentinel, XDR agent. Uses OpenAI GPT-4. Customer data not used for training. NRT analysis rules with AI for Pattern Matching and Anomaly Fusion
  • Defender XDR Suite: Unified XDR across MDO (Safe Attachments/Links, ZAP, AIR), MDE (Core DVM, ASR, NGP, EDR, AIR), MDCA (shadow IT discovery, info protection, SSPM, app governance, AI agent), MDI (sensors, proactive assessment, kill chain detection), Defender Vulnerability Management (CVE-based, CISA KEV), Defender Threat Intelligence (threat analytics, intel profiles/explorer/projects, reputation scoring). Cross-product: combined incidents, automatic response, attack disruption. Security Exposure Management (attack paths, critical asset rules, adversary simulations)

4. Compliance Solutions (20–25% of exam)

  • Compliance Principles: Six principles — Control, Transparency, Security, Legal Protections, No Content-Based Targeting, Benefit to Customer. Service Trust Portal hosts compliance docs, certifications, reports, regional/industry info (My Library for bookmarks)
  • Microsoft Priva: Privacy Risk Management (discover where private data lives, limit cross-boundary transfers). Subject Rights Requests (full workflow for individuals requesting access/deletion of personal data). Consent Management (track/manage user consent)
  • Microsoft Purview: Three pillars — Governance (Data Map, Unified Catalog, data quality), Compliance (Compliance Manager, Communication Compliance, eDiscovery, Audit, Insider Risk), Data Security (DLP, sensitivity labels, information protection, adaptive protection, DSPM). Data lifecycle: Know, Classify, Protect, Prevent, Govern
  • Compliance Manager: Compliance score = achieved points / total possible points. Prebuilt assessments for ISO 27001, GDPR, NIST, SOC 2, FedRAMP, HIPAA. Improvement actions with point values (Implemented=1.0, Tested=1.0, Unknown=0.0, Not implemented=0.0). Automated testing via Secure Score and Defender for Cloud
  • Data Classification: SITs — built-in (300+), named entity (people/addresses/medical), custom (regex/keywords), EDM (database exact match with salted hashes). Trainable classifiers (ML-based, pre-trained for harassment/profanity/threat/HR/finance/legal). Content Explorer (current state of labeled items). Activity Explorer (user actions on labels, 30-day window)
  • Sensitivity Labels: Persistent clear-text metadata, one per item. Actions: encrypt (specify users/groups/permissions), mark (watermark/header/footer), auto-apply (SITs/classifiers), protect containers (Teams/Groups/Sites), MIP SDK for third-party apps. Label scopes: Files, Emails, Meetings, Groups & sites
  • DLP: Deep content analysis across Exchange, SharePoint, OneDrive, Teams, endpoints (Windows/macOS), cloud apps, on-prem, Edge for Business. Actions: policy tip, block with override, hard block, lock/quarantine, hide in Teams. DLP for AI interactions (warn/block pasting sensitive data into ChatGPT etc.). Endpoint DLP: monitor copy/print/USB/network share. Teams DLP: policy tips on sensitive messages. Security Copilot integration: alert summarization + Alert Triage Agent
  • Insider Risk Management: Four principles — Transparency, Configurable, Integrated, Actionable. Workflow: Policies (templates for data theft, leaks, policy violations, AI usage, agents, priority users, healthcare, HR stressors) → Alerts → Triage → Investigate (user activity chart, content explorer, data risk graph with Sentinel) → Action (notification, eDiscovery escalation, forensic evidence). Adaptive Protection: ML-driven dynamic DLP/retention/CA controls based on risk level (Elevated/Moderate/Minor)
  • Records Management: Retention labels as records (no edit/delete) or regulatory records (strongest — cannot remove label). Disposition review, adaptive vs static scopes, preservation lock. eDiscovery tiers: Content Search (basic keyword), Standard (cases + holds), Premium (custodians, advanced analytics, review sets, redactions). Audit Standard (90 days), Premium (1 year+, up to 10 years, higher bandwidth API, custom policies, Copilot interaction logging)
  • DSPM & Data Security Investigations: DSPM — unified data security view across M365, Azure, Fabric, non-Microsoft (GCP, Snowflake, Databricks via partners). AI observability for agent activities. Data risk assessments, posture metrics. Data Security Investigations — vector search (meaning-based), categorization, examination (credentials/network/vulnerability scanning). Actions: soft purge or hard purge. Pay-as-you-go billing
  • Data Governance: Federated governance model (centralized standards + decentralized ownership). Data roles: consumers, owners, stewards, central data office. Microsoft Purview Data Map (scans/catalogs Azure, M365, on-prem sources, auto-discovers assets, classifies sensitive info, maps lineage). Unified Catalog (business-friendly view for discovering data assets). Governance Domains (organize by business concept: Marketing, Finance, Sales). Data Products (named, owned data assets serving specific use cases). Glossary Terms (business-language definitions). Critical Data Elements (CDEs with quality rules and access policies). Data Quality (no-code rules + AI-generated rules, scores at asset/product/domain levels)
  • Licensing Quick Reference: Conditional Access requires Entra P1. Risk-based CA, PIM, Identity Protection, Access Reviews require P2 (in E5). Defender for Office 365 Plan 1 (Safe Attachments/Links) in E3/Business Premium; Plan 2 (AIR, Threat Explorer, simulation) requires E5. Defender for Endpoint P2, Defender for Identity, Defender for Cloud Apps require E5/Defender Suite. Sentinel is pay-as-you-go Azure (not in M365 SKUs), but Defender alerts are free ingestion. Security Copilot included with E5/E7 starting 2025 or standalone SCUs. Auto-labeling, DLP for Teams/Endpoints, Insider Risk, Communication Compliance, eDiscovery Premium, Audit Premium, Priva require E5/Purview Suite. M365 E5 bundles best value: Entra P2 + full Defender XDR + full Purview Suite + Security Copilot

SC-900 Licensing Guide

Comprehensive License Reference — All Products, Tiers & Bundles

Module: SC-900 Licensing Guide

8 Product Families | Exam Reference

🎯 SC-900 Exam: Licensing Focus

What the exam actually tests about licensing:

  • High-level distinctions only — SC-900 tests what's included where, not obscure licensing details or pricing. You won't be asked dollar amounts.
  • Know your Entra tiers: Free (Security Defaults MFA) → P1 (Conditional Access, hybrid identity, dynamic groups, SSPR write-back) → P2 (PIM, Identity Protection, Access Reviews). This is the single most tested licensing distinction on the exam.
  • Know M365 E3 vs E5: E5 bundles Entra P2 + full Defender XDR suite + full Purview suite + Security Copilot. E3 stops at P1 + basic Defender + basic Purview.
  • Not everything is in M365: Defender for Cloud and Microsoft Sentinel are Azure-native services billed separately. They are not included in any M365 SKU.
  • Security Copilot is E5-included — starting 2025. For non-E5 tenants, it's consumption-based via Security Compute Units (SCUs).

Common question patterns:

  • "Which Entra ID license is required for Conditional Access?" → P1
  • "Which Entra ID license is required for Privileged Identity Management?" → P2
  • "Which M365 plan includes the full Microsoft Defender XDR suite?" → E5
  • "True or False: Microsoft Sentinel is included in Microsoft 365 E5." → False (Sentinel is an Azure service billed separately)
  • "A company uses Microsoft 365 Business Premium. Which Entra ID tier do they have?" → P1
  • "Which license is needed for auto-labeling in Microsoft Purview?" → E5 or Purview Suite add-on

📋 Real-World License Scenarios

Scenario 1: "Our org has M365 E3. A security team wants to use PIM and Identity Protection."

What's missing: E3 includes Entra ID P1. PIM and Identity Protection require Entra ID P2.

Options: (a) Upgrade users to M365 E5 (best value — also unlocks full Defender XDR + Purview Suite). (b) Add EMS E5 add-on to existing E3 (Entra P2 + Intune + more). (c) Purchase standalone Entra ID P2 licenses.

Scenario 2: "We use Microsoft 365 Business Premium. We need to prevent sensitive data from being shared in Teams chats."

What's missing: Business Premium has Entra P1 and basic DLP for Exchange/SharePoint, but Teams DLP requires M365 E5 or the Microsoft Purview Suite add-on.

Options: (a) Add Microsoft Purview Suite to existing Business Premium. (b) Migrate to M365 E5 for the full suite.

Scenario 3: "We have M365 E5. Our SOC wants to use Microsoft Sentinel for SIEM. Is it included?"

Answer: No. Sentinel is an Azure-native SIEM/SOAR billed pay-per-GB through Azure subscription. However, security alerts from Defender XDR, Defender for Cloud, and Defender components are ingested for free into Sentinel — you only pay for non-security logs and analytics.

Scenario 4: "We use M365 E3 and need to detect on-prem identity attacks (pass-the-hash, golden ticket, etc.)."

What's needed: Microsoft Defender for Identity — detects lateral movement, privilege escalation, and compromised identities via on-prem AD sensors. Requires M365 E5 or the Defender Suite add-on.

Scenario 5: "Our Entra ID Free tier users are getting MFA prompts, but we want more control — block logins from specific countries."

What's missing: Free tier only offers MFA via Security Defaults (on/off, no granularity). Conditional Access with location policies requires Entra ID P1. Upgrade path: M365 Business Premium or E3 (both include P1).

Scenario 6: "We have M365 E3. Legal needs eDiscovery with analytics, review sets, and custodian management."

What's missing: E3 includes eDiscovery Standard (content search, cases, holds). eDiscovery Premium (analytics, review sets, AI coding/summarization) requires M365 E5 or the Purview Suite add-on.

1. Microsoft Entra ID — Licensing Tiers

TierKey FeaturesIncluded In
Free User & group management, SSO, basic security reports, self-service password change (cloud only), MFA via Security Defaults Azure, M365, Dynamics 365 subscriptions (automatic)
P1 All Free + Conditional Access, hybrid identity (Entra Connect/Cloud Sync), dynamic groups, SSPR with write-back, MFA policies, Application Proxy, Microsoft Identity Manager M365 E3/F1/F3, M365 Business Premium, EMS E3
P2 All P1 + Identity Protection (risk-based CA, user/sign-in risk), Privileged Identity Management (JIT, time-bound, approval-based), Access Reviews, Entitlement Management M365 E5/E7, EMS E5, Microsoft Defender Suite
Entra Suite Requires P1 as prerequisite. Bundles: Entra Private Access, Entra Internet Access, Entra ID Governance, Entra ID Protection, Entra Verified ID (premium). Combines identity governance + network access + verification. Standalone add-on or M365 E7

Note: Custom roles (Entra RBAC) require P1 or P2. Entra Internet Access for Microsoft Services is included with P1/P2.

Entra Suite — What Each Product Does

  • Entra Private Access — Zero Trust VPN replacement. Routes private network traffic through Entra edge. Replaces legacy VPN.
  • Entra Internet Access — Secures outbound SaaS/web traffic with FQDN filtering, tenant restrictions, content filtering.
  • Entra ID Governance — Lifecycle workflows (joiner/mover/leaver), access reviews, entitlement management, automated provisioning.
  • Entra ID Protection — Risk-based detection (user risk + sign-in risk), automated remediation, integration with CA.
  • Entra Verified ID — Decentralized identity / verifiable credentials (premium capabilities in Suite).

3. Microsoft Defender XDR — Component Licensing

Defender for Office 365

PlanKey FeaturesIncluded In
Built-in Basic anti-malware, anti-spam, anti-phishing for all cloud mailboxes All M365 subscriptions
Plan 1 Safe Attachments, Safe Links, real-time detection, anti-phishing (advanced) M365 Business Premium, E3
Plan 2 All P1 + automated investigation & response (AIR), Threat Explorer, Attack Simulation Training, Threat Trackers, campaign views, XDR integration M365 E5/A5/G5, Defender Suite

Defender for Endpoint

PlanKey FeaturesIncluded In
Plan 1 Next-gen AV, attack surface reduction, endpoint detection & response (EDR) baseline, device control M365 E3 (Extra Features), Microsoft 365 Business Premium
Plan 2 All P1 + advanced EDR, automated investigation & response (AIR), threat analytics, threat & vulnerability management, APT hunting, behavioral sensors M365 E5, Defender Suite (E5 Security)

Other Defender Components

  • Defender for Identity — Detects identity attacks (lateral movement, privilege escalation) via on-prem AD sensors. Included in M365 E5 / Defender Suite.
  • Defender for Cloud Apps — CASB: Cloud Discovery (37,000+ apps), session controls, app governance, SSPM. Included in M365 E5 / Defender Suite.
  • Defender Vulnerability Management — Continuous asset discovery, risk-based prioritization. Built into Defender for Endpoint P2. Add-on for P1.
  • Defender Threat Intelligence — Intel profiles, threat analytics, IoC management. Included with Defender for Endpoint P2 / Defender Suite.

Microsoft Defender Suite (E5 Security)

Bundles: Defender for Office 365 Plan 2, Defender for Endpoint P2, Defender for Identity, Defender for Cloud Apps. Included with M365 E5 or available as standalone.

4. Microsoft Defender for Cloud — Plans

PlanKey FeaturesPricing
Foundational CSPM Secure Score, MCSB compliance assessment, security recommendations, multicloud visibility (AWS/GCP), network security map, regulatory compliance dashboard Free (enabled by default on Azure subscriptions)
Defender CSPM All Foundational + Agentless scanning, attack path analysis, cloud security graph, CIEM, sensitive data discovery, AI security posture, DevOps security Per-resource billing

5. Microsoft Sentinel

ModelDetails
Pay-as-you-go Pay per GB of data ingested into Log Analytics. SIEM analysis billed separately. No upfront commitment.
Capacity Reservations Commit to a tier (50-5000 GB/day) for up to 60% discount vs PAYG. Best for predictable volumes.
Free Data Sources Azure Activity Logs, O365 Audit Logs (SharePoint/Exchange/Teams), security alerts from Defender XDR, Defender for Cloud, Defender for Identity/Endpoint/Office/Cloud Apps, Sentinel Health — no ingestion charge for these data types.
Free Trial 31-day free trial with up to 10 GB/day of included data analysis.

Note: Sentinel is an Azure resource billed through Azure subscription. Not included in M365 E5. Raw logs from Defender components (beyond alerts) are paid ingestion.

6. Microsoft Security Copilot

Licensing ModelDetails
Security Compute Units (SCUs) Consumption-based model. Each SCU provides a pool of capacity for processing prompts. Provisioned through the Security Copilot portal. Pay per SCU provisioned.
Included with Microsoft 365 E5/E7 Starting 2025, Security Copilot is included with Microsoft 365 E5 and E7 licenses. Zero-click activation for eligible tenants — no manual SCU provisioning needed.
Standalone Non-E5 customers must manually provision SCUs and configure RBAC. Available as a paid add-on.

Note: SCUs determine throughput/capacity, not feature access. Available in both embedded (inside Defender/Entra/Sentinel) and standalone (dedicated portal) experiences.

Section Summary

  • Entra ID: Free (MFA via Security Defaults) → P1 (Conditional Access, hybrid identity, dynamic groups — in M365 E3/Business Premium) → P2 (PIM, Identity Protection, Access Reviews — in M365 E5) → Entra Suite (identity governance + network access + verification, requires P1)
  • M365 E3: Entra P1 + Defender for Office 365 P1 + manual sensitivity labels + eDiscovery Standard + Audit Standard
  • M365 E5: Entra P2 + full Defender XDR (MDO P2, MDE P2, MDI, MDCA, Vuln Mgmt) + full Purview Suite (auto-labeling, DLP for Teams/Endpoint, IRM, Comm Compliance, eDiscovery Premium, Audit Premium, Records, Compliance Manager, Priva) + Security Copilot — the most cost-effective bundle
  • Defender for Cloud: Foundational CSPM is free; per-resource Defender plans (servers, containers, databases, etc.) add workload protection — billed separately from M365
  • Sentinel: Pay-per-GB Azure SIEM/SOAR (not in M365 SKUs), but free ingestion for Defender alerts
  • Security Copilot: Consumption-based Security Compute Units (SCUs) or included with E5 starting 2025
  • Purview: E3 = manual labeling + manage; E5 = auto-labeling + ML + Insider Risk + Premium audit + Premium eDiscovery
  • E5 bundles deliver the best value — standalone add-ons exist for most missing E3 features (Defender for Office 365 P2, Defender for Endpoint P2, Purview Suite, etc.)
